Ministry of Industry: Shanghai Fish Market Business Regulations 120

The Shanghai Fish Market of the Ministry of Industry, after the responsible personnel such as the directors and supervisors and managers appointed by the ministry, will convene a board meeting within days to decide on the opening date and commence business immediately. The business regulations are recorded as follows:

Types of Business

Chapter 1: General Provisions, Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 22 of the Provisional Articles of Association of the Shanghai Fish Market of the Ministry of Industry. Article 2: The types of fish and seafood traded in the fish market are stipulated as follows: 1. Marine fish; 2. Freshwater fish; 3. Salted and dried fish; 4. Other aquatic products. Article 3: The daily opening and closing hours of the market shall be determined and announced by the fish market. Article 4: The holidays of the fish market are stipulated as follows: 1. National Day; 2. New Year's Day; 3. Days when businesses in Shanghai customarily close. The fish market may open on holidays if deemed necessary.

Qualifications for Brokers

Chapter 2: Brokers, Article 5: Fish market brokers are limited to citizens of the Republic of China. The number is tentatively set at ten. If necessary, it may be increased or decreased at any time. Article 6: Those who have any of the following circumstances shall not be fish market brokers: 1. Those without the capacity for civil conduct; 2. Those who have been declared bankrupt; 3. Those who have been deprived of public rights and have not yet been restored; 4. Those who have completed a sentence of imprisonment of one year or more, or who have not been five years after being pardoned; 5. Those who have been removed from the fish market for less than three years. Article 7: Anyone who wishes to become a fish market broker shall fill out a letter of application, a resume, together with documents proving experience in the fishing industry, and prepare a deposit of five thousand yuan, and a letter of guarantee from two established shops. These shall be submitted to the fish market for review and approval, and then presented to the Ministry of Industry for the issuance of a business license.

Broker Business

Article 8: Brokers shall be responsible to the fish market for all transactions arising from their transactions. Article 9: Brokers shall not use improper methods to participate in auctions. During auctions, they shall not use secret languages or codes. Article 10: Brokers may appoint agents to conduct their business. Article 11: When a broker appoints an agent, the agent's resume must be submitted to the fish market for review and approval before it becomes effective. When an agent is dismissed, the broker must report the reasons for the dismissal to the fish market for record. Article 12: Brokers must set up a business office within the location designated by the fish market. Article 13: The format of the account books and documents used by brokers for transactions shall be stipulated by the fish market and may be retrieved and inspected at any time. If there are any inquiries, they should be answered immediately. Article 14: Brokers and their agents shall be issued badges by the fish market. Those without badges shall not be allowed to participate in auctions. If lost or damaged, they should request a replacement. The badges received by brokers or agents shall not be lent or given to others.

Broker Closure

Article 15: Brokers must strictly abide by the rules and regulations of the fish market and shall not violate them. Article 16: When a broker closes their business, they must submit a letter stating the reasons for the closure and return the business license and entrance badge to the fish market. However, if there are outstanding transactions or unpaid payments, the business shall not be closed. Article 17: When a broker is subject to removal, if there are unfinished transactions, the broker shall settle them themselves. If they cannot be settled, the fish market shall designate another broker to settle them on their behalf. If there is any loss, it shall be borne by the broker. Article 18: If a broker violates any of the following circumstances, the fish market may temporarily suspend their transactions or remove them: 1. Failure to pay the price of goods when pursued in accordance with the provisions of Article 39, paragraph 1; 2. Delay in payment of the price of goods; 3. Actions that hinder the business of the fish market, with concrete evidence; 4. Failure to purchase fish from the fish market for more than ten months; 5. Monthly purchase of fish, the total value of which is less than 50 yuan; 6. Violation of the rules and regulations of the fish market.

Procedures for Consignment

Chapter 4: Transaction Methods, Article 21: Fish consigned for transaction shall be traded by the fish market upon presentation of a consignment note by the owner or their agent. The consignment note shall specify the type and quantity of the fish and its minimum selling price. If the price is not specified, the fish market may sell it at the usual price. Article 22: After the fish market receives the consignment note from the owner, if the fish has been landed and transported to the fish market, it shall immediately inspect, count, and issue a receipt. Article 23: The owner of the fish consigned for transaction shall not arbitrarily withdraw the consignment. However, this shall not apply in cases where there is no alternative and permission has been obtained from the fish market. For fish withdrawn from previous consignments, the corresponding handling fee shall still be paid. The amount shall be determined separately. Article 24: The fish consigned for transaction, which has been delivered to the fish market for counting and for which a receipt has been received, shall be the responsibility of the fish market for safekeeping. If there is any loss, it shall be compensated by the fish market. However, this shall not apply to the inevitable reduction in weight and losses due to weather conditions and force majeure. Fish that has not been landed and delivered to the fish market may be traded on the basis of samples. The owner shall be responsible for the safekeeping of such fish. Article 25: Fish consigned for transaction shall be sold by the fish market by auction. However, in any of the following circumstances, the fish market may sell it by other methods: 1. When it is deemed inappropriate to use the auction method in practice; 2. When the quantity of fish is too large or it arrives too late, making auction difficult; 3. When the use of the auction method may depress the price of the goods; 4. When it is deemed necessary to use other trading methods. Article 26: The language used in the auction shall be the language of the owner, but the commonly used language of Shanghai may be used as appropriate. Article 27: The fish market shall determine the order of auction based on the order in which the owners consigned the goods. Article 28: The fish market may refuse to trade fish if it has any of the following conditions: 1. It has rotted or is detrimental to hygiene; 2. It is prohibited by law to catch or sell it. Article 29: Only fish market brokers and agents may participate in auctions. Article 30: If a broker purchases fish outside the fish market in the Shanghai urban area without going through the fish market, the fish market shall, in addition to calculating the price of the fish and collecting the handling fee in accordance with the regulations, also have the power to remove them. Article 31: After a fish transaction is completed, the fish market shall immediately register it in the records. Article 32: If the fish market considers the auction price to be inappropriate, it may stop the auction at any time. Article 33: If the price of fish consigned for transaction is not specified quickly, the provisions of the preceding article shall apply. Article 34: After the transaction is completed and registered in the records, the fish market shall immediately send a settlement statement to both the owner and the broker. Neither party shall raise any objections to the confirmed transaction. Article 35: After the transaction is completed, the broker shall immediately inspect and receive the purchased fish and move it away from the auction site immediately. Article 36: Once the fish has been received, the broker shall be responsible for its safekeeping. The fish market shall not be liable for any losses. For fish that has not been landed and delivered to the fish market and is sold based only on samples, the broker shall also receive it immediately after the transaction is completed and move it away from the place where the fish is stored without delay. If there is any dispute regarding the receipt of such fish, it shall be resolved by the fish market. Both parties shall abide by it and shall not object. Article 37: If the broker refuses to receive and move the purchased fish without a legitimate reason, the broker shall be responsible for all losses.

Payment and Disputes

Article 38: The fish market shall pay the balance of the fish sale price to the owner on the same day, after deducting the handling fee and other payable items. Article 39: The price of fish owed by brokers to the fish market shall be settled every five days. However, in any of the following circumstances, the fish market may pursue it at any time: 1. The amount of unpaid fish exceeds the prescribed maximum limit. The maximum limit shall be determined and announced by the fish market. 2. When a broker is removed or suspended from participating in auctions. Article 40: If a broker is unable to pay the amount owed, the fish market may deduct it from the deposit. If it is not enough, it shall be recovered from the guarantor. Article 41: For transactions made by a broker entrusted by a customer, the fish market only recognizes the entrusted broker as the principal of the transaction. All matters related to the transaction of the entrusting party shall be handled directly with the entrusted broker, and the fish market shall not be involved in any way. Chapter 5: Arbitration, Article 42: When a broker or consignor has a dispute arising from the consignment relationship and requests arbitration from the fish market, the fish market shall temporarily appoint arbitrators from among the staff and members of the brokers' association. Events involving personal or family interests shall be recused.

Transaction Handling Fees

Chapter 6: Handling Fees, Article 43: The fish market shall charge the owner handling fees for fish consigned for transaction at the following rates: 1. Seafood fish and shellfish: 6% of the total price; 2. Freshwater fish: 5% of the total price; 3. Salted and dried fish and shellfish and other aquatic products: 5% of the total price. Article 44: The fish market shall distribute the handling fees collected to brokers at the following rates: 1. Seafood fish and shellfish: 3% of the total price; 2. Freshwater fish: 2.5% of the total price; 3. Salted and dried fish and shellfish and other aquatic products: 2.5% of the total price. Article 45: The fish market may change the rates stipulated in the preceding two articles at any time if it deems it necessary and shall report to the Ministry of Industry for record. Chapter 7: Supplementary Provisions, Article 46: For all matters not stipulated in these rules, the fish market may temporarily announce and implement them. Article 47: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Brokers Association

Chapter 2: Brokers' Association, Article 19: Brokers shall organize a brokers' association to promote their common business interests and correct their malpractices. Article 20: The rules and decisions made by the brokers' association shall take effect only after being approved by the fish market. If the fish market considers them inappropriate, it may order the brokers' association to make corrections in whole or in part.

City Chamber of Commerce Letter Requesting: Correction of Illegal Measures by the Vehicle Committee; Substitute Writing of Debt Acknowledgements Infringing on Creditor Rights; Unauthorized Penalties Encroaching on Court Authority 128

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a letter to the Public Works Department, requesting correction of the illegal measures taken by the Vehicle Committee against vehicle owners. The letter stated:

"To the esteemed Public Works Department:

On the 17th of this month, we received a letter from the Manpower Rickshaw Industry Association stating that, concerning the special district rickshaw owners association, last year the Vehicle Committee proposed a rent reduction, which led to many disputes. The Public Works Department repeatedly convened meetings of rickshaw owner representatives with the Vehicle Committee on an equal basis. The result was an agreement to collect a daily rent of 85 cents in silver dollars, including the collection of mutual aid fees for rickshaw pullers. Other items such as rickshaw puller loans, rent arrears, and room fees were also allowed to be collected separately. Later, because rickshaw pullers did not have silver dollars to pay the rent, it was agreed to change the daily collection to 12 cents in small silver coins.

This November, after our country implemented the new currency system, the association immediately sent a letter to the branch office stating that due to the depreciation of silver dollars and the high price of small silver coins, the original rent of 85 cents in silver dollars should be changed to 10.6 cents in small silver coins per day, and no excess should be collected. This was immediately forwarded to all vehicle owners, with instructions to inform the lessees to comply.

However, a few unscrupulous rickshaw pullers, who had long-standing grudges against vehicle owners or lessees, often used this as an opportunity to make false accusations. Also, when vehicle owners or lessees sought to recover debts or collect room fees, it caused dissatisfaction, leading to hasty reports and false accusations of excessive collection. The Vehicle Committee did not investigate in detail, and anyone who made a complaint was summoned, and anyone summoned was penalized. Each penalty was 10 or 20 dollars, and more were extrapolated. If they refused to pay, their licenses would be confiscated for a month according to the number of penalties. If they were dissatisfied and applied for a review, they would inevitably be penalized double upon a second summons, regardless of whether we were right. Furthermore, if they were away on business during the summons period and could not attend on time, they would be considered disobedient and penalized double.

Even more shocking, in the case of Luan Lizhen, the lessee of vehicle owner Wang Shengji, because of collecting arrears each shift, a rickshaw puller reported excessive rent collection. When both parties were summoned to the scene, Luan Lizhen repeatedly clarified that the collected money was actually owed by the rickshaw puller, and the rickshaw puller also admitted owing money. It seemed that there should be no problem. However, the Vehicle Committee insisted on its own way, not only fining Wang Shengji 80 dollars but also forcing Luan Lizhen to sign eight debt acknowledgments for the rickshaw puller and give them to the rickshaw puller. The rickshaw puller owed Luan money at that time without any receipts. Now, even if it were repaid in full, there would be no need to sign a receipt. Moreover, the association did not receive a penny, yet it wrote in large characters, 'The owed money has been received in full.' Its illegal abuse of power is chilling.

Currently, vehicle owners are reporting repeatedly that the Vehicle Committee's penalties are even more severe than before, occurring several or dozens of times a day. It is estimated that the penalized vehicles account for almost one-tenth of the total. The reason is that the committee does not consider the truth and relies solely on the rickshaw pullers' one-sided statements, believing them to be accurate. Rickshaw pullers also believe that false accusations are not a crime, so they are becoming more frequent. Otherwise, how could the special district vehicle owners, who have eyes and ears, still dare to greedily overcharge a little rent in the midst of so many penalty sounds, risking heavy penalties or confiscation of their licenses for a month? Even a foolish vehicle owner would not be so foolish.

We believe that since the Public Works Department established the Vehicle Committee for the special district manpower rickshaw industry, the implementation of new regulations has become increasingly severe, and the suffering endured has been unbearable. Now, forcibly imposing penalties and compelling receipts, the oppression and destruction are limitless. The future of the manpower rickshaw industry is unimaginable. It is almost inevitable that they will go bankrupt.

We have always admired your association for leading the merchants and supporting various industries, so we should truthfully submit this to you for review and promptly forward it to the Public Works Department, asking them to correct the Vehicle Committee's various illegal actions, so that vehicle owners can avoid endless losses and prevent the expansion of disputes. Vehicle owners will be fortunate, and society will be fortunate. We are eagerly awaiting your response."

Attached was a photographic copy of a receipt.

Upon investigation, the association pointed out that the Vehicle Committee listened only to one side and arbitrarily imposed penalties in various situations, as evidenced by the rickshaw puller's admission that he owed Luan Lizhen money. However, the Vehicle Committee actually wrote a receipt on their behalf, forcing the cancellation of the debt. With the Vehicle Committee's written receipt as evidence, it is not an empty accusation. This alone demonstrates that their daily work does indeed exceed the scope and that the legitimate interests of vehicle owners have not been considered. Moreover, according to the committee's authority, there is no reason to arbitrarily penalize vehicle owners. This encroaches on the authority of the court. The committee's actions raise serious legal issues.

Accordingly, we have attached a photographic copy and respectfully request that your department severely reprimand the Vehicle Committee for all unreasonable measures taken in the past and ensure that they are corrected. This is our utmost hope.

After Settlement of the Owed Money from the China Commercial Bank: Lu Shaotang Surrenders to the Police Station for Interrogation; Public Prosecution for Embezzlement of Business Still Proceeds; Court Debate Concluded Yesterday, Awaiting Sentence 130

Lu Shaotang, a real estate tycoon from Suzhou, had a close relationship with Chuan Xiao'an, the former president of the China Commercial Bank. Two years ago, he suggested to Chuan that a branch of the China Commercial Bank be established in Suzhou, and he recommended his son, Lu Bingsheng, as the general manager of the branch. Chuan accepted his suggestion but felt that Bingsheng was too young, so he appointed Lu to the position of general manager and gave Bingsheng the position of deputy manager to assist his father.

Lu originally founded the Guixing Real Estate Company at No. 207 Tianjin Road. After becoming the general manager of the Suzhou branch, he proposed to Chuan, with the latter's consent, to establish a communications office for the Suzhou branch within the Guixing Real Estate Company to facilitate the handling of public and private affairs. All banknotes paid to the branch by the head office were handled by the Guixing Company, and the Lu family used this financial power to operate their real estate business.

By the beginning of January this year, they had misappropriated 510,000 banknotes. In addition, the Guixing Company owed the China Commercial Bank more than 400,000. At this time, it was the end of the lunar year, and real estate prices in the market were falling. Lu's business was almost a complete failure. Therefore, Chuan Xiao'an demanded repayment from Lu Shaotang.

After gradually raising 680,000, Chuan not only cleared their current account debts but also used the remaining 170,000 to offset the misappropriated banknotes. However, there was still a shortage of 239,000 yuan. After pursuing repayment until May without success, Chuan Xiao'an reported the matter to the police station. Lu hid in advance, and his son, Bingsheng, was often detained and brought before the First Special District Local Court, which found him guilty of embezzlement of business and sentenced him to one year and six months in prison. Meanwhile, the court issued an arrest warrant for Lu Shaotang, who was at large.

However, Lu Bingsheng was dissatisfied with the first-instance judgment and is still appealing in the third instance. In recent months, Lu Shaotang has repeatedly asked relatives and friends to mediate with the China Commercial Bank. Now, the private prosecution regarding compensation for the missing banknotes has been resolved peacefully. The China Commercial Bank officially sent a letter to the police station a few days ago, stating that Lu had repaid the money. However, the police station stated that even if the private prosecution part of the case was settled, the public prosecution for embezzlement of business must still proceed according to the law and is not affected by the settlement.

In response to the letter from Lu's defense lawyer, Lu knew that he could not continue to live as a fugitive, so he surrendered to the police station at 5:45 AM yesterday. He was then sent to the First Special Court, where Judge Feng Shide opened the court for interrogation. Lu was already 68 years old, with white hair and beard. After the prosecuting lawyer Wang Yaotang of the police station presented the case, he began to defend himself at length, saying that the 239,000 yuan owed was actually the Guixing Company's debt to the China Commercial Bank and not the amount of missing banknotes. He claimed that when he gradually handed over 680,000 to Chuan Xiao'an, he had declared to Chuan that he would first repay the 510,000 yuan missing banknotes, and the remaining amount would be used to settle the accounts of current debtors, but Chuan had misunderstood and cleared the current accounts first. The remaining outstanding amount of 239,000 was treated as still as missing cash, but it has since been repaid. He also claimed that the accounts of Guixing Company, China Commercial Bank, and Suzhou branch were not fully compliant, all due to Chuan Xiao'an's excessive trust in him.

Judge Feng said that Lu Shaotang had indeed used the banknotes deposited by the China Commercial Bank in the Guixing Company for private purposes and could not escape the responsibility for embezzlement of business. He could not attempt to evade responsibility by compensating for it afterward. Therefore, after repeatedly questioning Lu, the defense lawyer and the police station lawyer debated successively. The China Commercial Bank also appointed lawyer E Sen to represent the bank in court, stating the process of the defendant's repayment and settlement. The court then declared the debate closed and adjourned until next Tuesday morning for sentencing. Lu Shaotang paid a bail of 50,000 yuan. Before the bail was secured, he was temporarily released into the custody of his defense lawyer.

According to the Japanese-language Daily News, at 10:10 PM on the 18th, the watchman of Hongkou Park suddenly discovered a man who had taken poison next to a chair near the ball field. Xu Qizhong, Son of Xu Guannan, Accused of Fraud, Escorted from Hangzhou to Shanghai; Wang Bingzhong Accuses Xu of Borrowing 40,000 Yuan Using Fake Land Deeds as Collateral; Xu Admits to Only Using 3,000 Yuan but Was Coerced into Signing the IOU 131

—Plaintiff, a Portuguese National, Briefly Argues with Police Station Lawyer—

Two weeks ago, a large advertisement appeared in the advertisement columns of major newspapers in this city, namely, Wang Pingsong (also known as Wang Bingzhong)'s notice offering a reward for the arrest of Xu Qizhong, the son of Xu Guannan. It is now known that Xu Qizhong had his actions monitored and his residence restricted by the Public Security Bureau in Hangzhou. They also notified the Chengdu Road Police Station, which dispatched detectives Yang Xinzheng and Western detective Haruo, who traveled to Hangzhou and escorted Xu to Shanghai the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Criminal Division Eight of the First Special Court, where he was charged with fraud under Article 339 of the Criminal Law and forgery of documents under Article 210 of the same law.

Both the plaintiff and the defendant hired lawyers to attend court. According to police station lawyer Zhang Dayin, who rose to present the case, on October 16, the victim Wang Bingzhong reported to the police station that the defendant Xu Qizhong had borrowed 40,000 yuan from him on May 22nd and signed an IOU at his office at No. 28, Fuming Village, 424 Foch Road. At the time, in addition to the original defendant, there were also guarantors Shen Shouheng and lawyers Shen Yiqian and Shen Boxiong signing the IOU on site.

The defendant used three land deeds as collateral (two on Hongqiao Road, one on Yangshupu Road), stating that the mortgage period was one year and six months, with interest starting at 1.5% per month. At the time, Wang felt that these collaterals were not enough, so the defendant promised to provide an additional 100,000 yuan in shares of the Nanshi Water and Electricity Company in the future. Wang then issued eight checks from the Shanghai Bank, each worth 5,000 yuan, dated May 22. According to Wang, the money had already been withdrawn from the bank by the defendant.

Later, Wang became suspicious of the land deeds that Xu had provided and investigated with the Land Bureau. According to Director Jin Liren's instructions, all three land deeds were forgeries. Wang then pursued the guarantor Shen Shouheng, and entrusted lawyer Chen to send a letter to the defendant, setting a deadline for returning the money. Since there was no reply, Wang offered a reward and advertised in the newspaper for Xu's arrest. The Hangzhou Public Security Bureau found out about Xu's whereabouts and restricted the defendant's residence, notifying the police station, which escorted Xu to Shanghai yesterday.

However, according to the defendant's statement at the police station, it was true that he borrowed money from the plaintiff, but he only received 3,220 yuan, not 40,000 yuan. The IOU was signed because he was in urgent need. The guarantor Shen Shouheng was a friend of Wang Bingzhong. The police station had not investigated the case in detail, so they requested that the charges be changed.

Next, Wang Bingzhong, 32 years old, Portuguese, born in Macau, residing at No. 28 Fuming Village, Foch Road, stated that he lent the defendant 40,000 yuan on September 22 and had the defendant sign an IOU in his own handwriting, witnessed and signed by the guarantor Shen Shouheng and two lawyers. The defendant used three land deeds as collateral. At the time, I also asked for additional collateral. The defendant agreed to provide additional collateral in the form of shares of the water company and grain warrants. I then issued eight Shanghai Bank checks, totaling 40,000 yuan, and the defendant signed and sealed the back of the checks to withdraw the money. Later, the defendant did not send the additional collateral, so I sent a letter to urge him.

He replied that he could not do so because his father refused to hand them over. I became suspicious of the previously delivered land deeds and sent them to the Land Bureau for investigation, which confirmed that they were forgeries. Later, the defendant suddenly disappeared. I then posted an advertisement for his arrest.

Judge Liu then questioned him as to how much he had on deposit at the Shanghai Bank when the checks were issued, and when the money for the checks was withdrawn. Wang refused to answer and was stubborn in his statement, leading to an argument with the police station lawyer. Judge Liu then instructed Wang that this was a Chinese court, and he should maintain order in the courtroom. Since he was the victim, he should answer the questions as fully as possible during the evidence investigation so that the case could be clarified. Wang complied.

When questioned, the defendant Xu Qizhong stated that he was introduced to Wang by Shen Shouheng. Since March of this year, he had borrowed a total of more than 1,000 yuan from Wang. On May 22, he borrowed more than 1,700 yuan from Wang at Wang's home in Fuming Village, Foch Road.

At that time, there were only Wang, Shen, and myself. At the time, Wang and others used some means to ask me to sign a pre-written IOU before handing me a check for 1,700 yuan from Shanghai Bank, which I went to withdraw. Therefore, up to the time of signing the IOU, I had only received a total of 3,220 yuan in loans and nothing about 40,000 yuan. I was coerced into signing the IOU for 40,000 yuan.

One of the lawyers came out of another room afterward and signed on the IOU. I do not know about the eight Shanghai Bank checks presented by the plaintiff. All three land deeds also belonged to Wang himself, who told me to admit that they were mine. After signing, Shen Shouheng and I went out together in a car. At the time, I thought that Wang's methods were like kidnapping, and I wanted to report it to the police station, but Shen threatened me, so I did not dare to report it. Also, the reply letter presented by Wang was also written by Wang when the IOU was signed, with the dates reversed to be my reply letter. All these methods were pre-planned. Later, I suddenly received a letter from lawyer Chen, setting a deadline of 24 hours for a reply. I was frightened and went to Hangzhou. I am only 22 years old and have limited knowledge, so I was fooled. Last year, at the end of the year, I also borrowed 5,000 yuan from Wang, and Wang requested the court to mediate, suing for 15,000 yuan. At that time, I did not appear in court, and Shen Shouheng appointed a lawyer to represent me in court, admitting 25,000 yuan. After the mediation was successful, it was repaid.

Judge Liu reviewed the statements and instructed Xu to post a bail of 40,000 yuan. The case was rescheduled for further hearing next Saturday.

After the Death of Gao Yunsun's Eldest Son, a Woman Sues, Requesting Confirmation of Granddaughter, Claiming to Be Born by Gao's Son 135

Gao Yunsun, a native of this county and head of the accounting department of the Zhengming Bank on Ningbo Road, is over sixty years old and has a modest family fortune. His eldest son, Gao Yuelun, worked at the Mccarley Bank. On October 3 of this year, his stomach burst, and medical treatment was ineffective, so he died. Recently, a local woman, Qian Meifen (32 years old, residing at No. 5 Zhaoqing Lane, Chengdu Road), claiming to be Yuelun's wife and that she had two daughters, the eldest daughter, Mei Jun, who is eight years old, and the youngest daughter, Mei Lin, who is only one year old and still in swaddling clothes, requested Gao Yunsun to recognize them. Gao refused, so she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Gao, requesting confirmation that Mei Jun and Mei Lin were his granddaughters.

The reason given was that after the plaintiff married Gao Yuelun, she gave birth to two daughters. When the defendant's wife was alive, she loved the eldest daughter Mei Jun very much, and the defendant often took her home. When Mei Jun was two years old, the aunt (i.e., the defendant's wife) died. This October, her husband Yuelun also died. The defendant listened to the words of his relatives and cut off the plaintiff's support. She sent a lawyer's letter to question him, but he did not recognize the plaintiff's right to raise the two daughters, etc. Because she was unable to pay the litigation fees, she temporarily reserved the right to do so, and first filed this lawsuit for confirmation, requesting confirmation that Gao Mei Jun and Gao Mei Lin are the defendant's granddaughters, etc.

The court granted the request. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Daxi opened the Civil Division Thirteen and summoned the defendant Gao Yunsun, who hired lawyer Zhang Ji to attend court. According to his defense, his son Yuelun had never taken a concubine outside, so how could there be children? Even if there was a concubine affair, it must be legally recognized before any kinship would be established. Therefore, he completely denied what the plaintiff said and requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed. After Judge Huang questioned him, the case was adjourned for another hearing at a later date.

Accusation of a Rebellious Son Beating His Mother; His Speech Incoherent, Seeming to Have a Mental Illness 136

Madam Gu Qian, a local old woman, residing at No. 20, Lane 1177, Xujiahui Road, French Concession, in her own house, is 81 years old this year, a Catholic, and quite wealthy. She has an only son, named Gu Hongxiang, also known as Fengxiang, who is 37 years old this year. He does not engage in proper work and is solely occupied with wandering about outside, either staying in inns or living in grand hotels, appearing to suffer from a mental illness. He spends his days squandering the ancestral property, often extorting money from his mother for his use. When his wishes are not fulfilled, he resorts to violence, doing all sorts of things. The day before yesterday (the 17th), at about 10 a.m., Gu Hongxiang again returned home to demand 10,000 yuan from his mother, as well as the land price receipts and letters for the land on Rue Lupan, Datok Fang, which the Public Works Department had acquired for road construction. Madam Qian refused to agree, and Hongxiang immediately became violent, slapping his old mother's face twice. After the assault, he turned and left. Madam Qian, considering her rebellious son's unlawful behavior and frequent assaults on his elders, feared the consequences and immediately reported the matter to the Beidang Road French Police Station, requesting an investigation. Detective Liu Kunbao went to arrest Gu Hongxiang, and the next day, he was sent to the Special Second Court, where Judge Qiu heard the case in the eighth civil chamber. The representative of the Police Department, lawyer Fei Xizhen, presented the case, requesting that it be tried according to Articles 280 and 281 of the Criminal Law. Subsequently, the plaintiff, Madam Gu Qian, recounted the defendant's violent acts, stating that over the past two years, more than 20,000 yuan had been spent, as evidenced by account books, which were submitted for inspection. Lawyer Zhu Yisheng, representing her, further described the defendant's past violent acts. When questioned, the defendant, Gu Hongxiang, stated that all the ancestral property of the people was managed by his mother, who gave him 300 yuan per month for his use. However, that was not enough for the people to use, and it would be best if she gave him 500 yuan, or even 5,000 yuan, each month. The judge asked what his monthly expenses were that required such a large sum. Gu Hongxiang replied that his expenses were very large, including the expenses of the whole world and the whole of China, his speech incoherent. The court adjourned the hearing to the 21st. The "Great America Evening News" reports that Western Police Head Peter of the Jiading Road Police Station and probationary Police Head Jute are accused of throwing beggar Ma Debiao into the Hongkou creek on December 1st, causing bodily harm, and Ma subsequently died in the hospital. The two of them then rescued the person to the shore. Yang Qingchang, Son of Former Zhejiang Military Governor Yang Shande, Accused of Breach of Contract; Plaintiffs are Yang Fuchen and Others, Representatives of the Clan, Accusing Him of Failing to Compile the Clan Genealogy and Fulfill the Contract 138

The late former Zhejiang Military Governor Yang Shande had a close friendship with Jewish millionaire Silas Aaron Hardoon, the owner of Aili Garden. Therefore, he entrusted his youngest son, Qingchang, to be raised in his garden, making Hardoon and Madame Luo Jialing his adoptive parents and guardians. Later, after Yang died, Yang's eldest son, Qingwei (style name Jingru), had a lawsuit with Qingchang over the division of the inheritance. At that time, Qingchang was still a child, so Hardoon, as his guardian, reached a settlement with Qingzheng to end the lawsuit. Not long after, Qingwei also passed away without any offspring, so his nephew, Yang Weizu, inherited his estate. Although Qingchang was dissatisfied, he suppressed his feelings. Now, Qingchang is 22 years old and has been cohabitating with Hardoon's adopted daughter, Ms. Chen, at No. 3, Ci Huili, Seymour Road, and has already had a child, but has not yet gone through the marriage formalities, which has caused considerable criticism from the Yang clan in his native Anqing. In April last year, the Yang clan discussed compiling the clan genealogy, and made quite critical remarks about Qingchang's marriage and childbirth. When Qingchang heard about this, he immediately sought to remedy the situation. He appointed clan representatives Yang Fuchen, Yang Yiqi, and Yang Xianbo, who came to Shanghai from Anhui, to negotiate. After discussions, the representatives were to find a way to complete the marriage formalities between Yang and Ms. Chen, so that the name of his child could also be included in the clan genealogy, and Qingchang would bear all the costs of compiling the genealogy and serve as the highest authority in charge of the compilation. Both parties immediately signed a contract as evidence. Later, Qingchang wanted to use the clan's influence to overturn the previous case in which Yang Weizu had inherited his brother Qingzheng's estate, and even wanted to recover a portion of the property that Qingzheng had obtained in the lawsuit with him, so he entered into another cooperation agreement with Yang Fuchen and the other two, entrusting Yang Fuchen and others to handle three matters: 1. Correcting Yang Weizu's illegal inheritance and management of property from Yang Qingzheng. 2. Revoking Hardoon's unfavorable promises made in court on behalf of Qingchang as his guardian. 3. Seeking compensation from Qingzheng's estate for the 1,000 shares of the Nanyang Company that Qingzheng had illegally occupied in Qingchang's name. If all three matters were successful, the benefits Qingchang would receive would be more than 200,000 yuan. Therefore, in the cooperation agreement, the rights to be obtained by Yang Fuchen and the other two were 10% of the future proceeds to be paid by Qingchang as remuneration, and another 10% to be transferred to the Yang Sizhitang clan as a public benefit. In addition, all expenses for the three representatives' travel to Shanghai and to and from Anhui, Shanghai, and Hangzhou would be provided by Qingchang, and the agreement stipulated that neither party could breach the contract halfway, or they would have to compensate for the losses. Unexpectedly, since the signing of the agreement, Yang Qingchang has neither borne the costs of compiling the genealogy nor assumed the highest position, allowing the genealogy work to be abandoned halfway. As for the three matters stipulated in the other agreement, he has also delayed them indefinitely without any intention of proceeding. Therefore, Yang Fuchen and the others believe that Qingchang has breached the contract and have hired lawyer Li Lin to file a lawsuit against Yang Qingchang in the First Special District Local Court for breach of contract, requesting a judgment ordering him to compensate for actual losses of 3,949.91 yuan and to bear the litigation costs. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Hui summoned them, and the defendant also hired a lawyer to represent him. After the court investigated the case, it was ordered that Yang Qingchang be summoned to court for further questioning on a later date.

Breaking a Lamp at a Beef Stall; Shaoxing Opera Troupe Stages an All-Out Brawl; Gangsters Wield Knives and Axes to Take Advantage of the Situation and Avenge Personal Grudges; Crown Prince Falls to the Ground Injured, "Willow Fate" Performance Suspended 139

The Taipinglou Teahouse, located at No. 60, Caishi Road, French Concession, is owned by Zhang Jinquan from Pudong. It used to also have a Tanhuang theater, but recently invited a Shaoxing troupe to perform Yue Opera, commonly known as "Didu Ban Shaoxing Opera." The troupe leader, Lou Gaofeng, is 29 years old and plays the role of a "xusheng" (bearded male character). Because of his superb artistry, he has a position similar to that of Tan Xinpei in the Peking Opera world. As a result, since the performance began, the business has been quite prosperous. Today, the contract expires, and they will move to the North City to perform. At 8:30 p.m. on the 13th of this month, Lou Gaofeng ordered his 12-year-old apprentice, the girl Zhou Lingzhi, to go to the

beef stall set up by Zhu Rongkui at the intersection of Route Lafayette, south of the Taipinglou,

to buy beef. Lingzhi obeyed the order and went to buy the beef. Unexpectedly, when she arrived next to the beef stall, she accidentally knocked over and broke the kerosene lamp that was lit on the stall. The stall owner, Zhu Yingkui, said to Lingzhi, "This lamp cost one yuan when it was originally bought from overseas, and now you must compensate for the lamp price of eight jiao." Lingzhi replied that she didn't have any money on her and would go and call her master to acknowledge the compensation. Zhu Rongkui then took the broken kerosene lamp with Lingzhi to the Taipinglou Teahouse to ask her master for compensation. When they arrived at the entrance, Lingzhi called her master, Lou Gaofeng, to come outside and

negotiate compensation

with the beef stall owner Zhu Rongkui. At that time, Lou Gaofeng, because Zhu had demanded eight jiao in compensation, immediately agreed to compensate half a yuan, four jiao. At that time, Zhu still thought he was losing too much, and was still hesitating. Lou Gaofeng, because he was playing the crown prince in the Yue Opera "Willow Fate" that night, was about to go on stage, and time was short, so he couldn't talk for a long time. He told Zhu to wait for him to finish singing and come off stage before discussing it further. Without waiting for Zhu's reply, he turned and went inside. Unexpectedly, at that moment, Wang Peisheng, a local gangster in the area (20 years old, from Changzhou, living at No. 1, Weiyuanli, near Route Lafayette), found out that Lou Gaofeng

had not greeted

them, the local gangsters, before he started singing at the Taipinglou, and held a grudge. Now seeing that his apprentice had caused trouble, he could take this opportunity to get revenge and extort money to vent his anger. So he snatched the broken kerosene lamp from Zhu Rongkui's hand and went straight into the backstage of the Taiping Teahouse to find Lou Gaofeng to argue and demand compensation. Lou said that this was a trivial matter, what did it have to do with him, and severely rebuked him and ordered him to be driven out. Wang was enraged and added fuel to the fire. He went outside for no more than five minutes and gathered more than a dozen of his accomplices, Tang Xiaokai, Liu Xiaokun, etc., each armed with axes, iron rods, etc., and rushed to the Taipinglou to seek revenge on Lou Gaofeng. At that time, Lou Gaofeng, playing

the crown prince in "Willow Fate",

had just followed the other actors and the extras playing civil and military officials out of the stage door from the stage, and was about to start singing. Wang Peisheng and several other troublemakers jumped onto the stage and blew Lou's head with axes. Fortunately, Lou was wearing a stage helmet (made of copper, etc.) and quickly dodged. A piece of the helmet corner had been chopped off, and the axe had already been slammed into the door panel. Lou had already dodged into the backstage, and Wang and others followed in, cutting Lou twice on the back with an axe. Then they dispersed and fled with a roar. Lou fell to the ground, and the play also

stopped performing due to the riot.

His companions reported the incident to the police station, and detectives rushed to the scene, but the culprits had already fled without a trace. The injured person was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. However, the owner of the Taipinglou, Zhang Jinquan, because Lou's opera troupe had been profitable since it started performing, but refused to stay when the contract expired, harbored a grudge. At the time of the incident, he did not come out to stop them, allowing the thugs to cause trouble. The police station sent detectives to summon Zhang and the beef stall owner to the police station for questioning. At the same time, they ordered detectives to investigate and arrest the criminals. However, after the incident, all the criminals scattered and hid. On the morning of the 18th, Detective Sui Wenzhi learned that the ringleader, Wang Peisheng,

was hiding in his home.

So he went to the address with detectives Yang Weishan and others to arrest him. When they arrived, Wang was hiding in the room. His wife came out to answer, saying that Wang was not at home. The detectives then used a trick to lure him, pretending to be sent by Little Ningbo, saying that they had something to ask Wang to help with. Wang heard the voice in the room and thought that a business opportunity had come, so he could not miss it, so he came out to greet them. The detectives then arrested him and took him to the police station. Under questioning, Wang admitted that he had gathered a gang and injured people with an axe, but although he held an axe, his hand was weak and he did not cut anyone, but it was Liu Xiaokun, who was on the run,

who cut Lou.

The police chief ordered him to be detained. Yesterday, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Chamber of the Special Second Court. Lawyer Yuan Jiahong of the Police Department presented the case, stating that the defendant had been arrested for the crime of injury, the victim was being treated in the hospital, and his injuries were very serious. The Police Department still needed to investigate and arrest the fleeing criminals, and requested an extension. Judge Sun Pengham approved the request after questioning the defendant Wang Peisheng. Wang's statements were evasive. The court ruled that the case would be adjourned and reinvestigated before another hearing. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Madame Maurice Talks About Her Travels; Not for Exploration But to Broaden Her Horizons; A Short Rest Before Three More Years 140

The "China Press" reports that Madame Maurice from New York City loves to travel. In the past seven years, she has traveled to various countries and experienced many dangerous situations. She recently arrived in Shanghai and is staying at the Cathay Hotel. She will travel north to visit the old capital on Saturday and Sunday. Madame Maurice is light in stature and gentle in demeanor, and one would never believe that she is an explorer, let alone that she gets up at 3 a.m. every morning and walks 23 miles a day for weeks on end. Nor would one believe that she has ventured deep into Tibet and traveled through the remote, uninhabited parts of the western Himalayas in India, riding in an ox cart during the day and sleeping in a tent at night, for four months on end. Moreover, her travels are all done alone, with only local people as guides. After enjoying a year of civilized life, Madame Maurice plans to return to uninhabited areas and continue her travels. Madame Maurice's travels are not for exploration, but merely to broaden her horizons. She has been traveling since childhood. In 1929, she visited India and, while viewing the high mountains, had the idea of following in the footsteps of Marco Polo. Two years later, she set off from London, passing through Darjeeling and entering Tibet, but at a point three stations away from Lhasa, Tibetan officials forced her to turn back. This time, she has been traveling for 18 months. She initially planned to cross Persia with a camel train, but the Persian government did not allow her to travel outside of the motor roads. According to Madame Maurice, Persia's motor roads are 6,000 miles long and have been built in recent years, with police strictly guarding them. The Persian government is very suspicious of travelers, especially women traveling alone in remote areas, fearing that they might secretly carry away recently excavated treasures. Madame Maurice, finding that she was being watched wherever she went, left Persia and traveled to Java, Bali, and Sumatra, and then returned to India. In India, Madame Maurice went through many setbacks before obtaining a travel permit. Then she went to various parts rarely visited by humans. Her horses often walked for several days to find grass and fodder, for four months on end. The journey was full of hardships. When she reached a place north of Lahore, she was stopped by the authorities and turned back to Kashmir. After ten days, she saw Tangchenjunga Mountain and Everest Mountain, and admired their magnificent mountain peaks. During this trip, she never went below 16,000 feet for two weeks, but because it was her first time, her strength was exhausted, and she wanted to collapse and lie down. The men who accompanied her felt lazy and tired, because at this altitude, it was not easy to boil water and cook food. Then she traveled about 500 miles over the Himalayas and walked about 400 miles. Madame Maurice said that traveling in the uninhabited parts of the world is like entering a world of floods, and the most beautiful scenery is the mountain colors at sunset. Although Madame Maurice's travels are only for leisure and have no other special purpose, she has written a book, one recording the wonders of the Himalayas, and one recording her experiences in Tibet. This is Madame Maurice's first visit to Shanghai. After staying in Beiping for a few months, she plans to visit Shanghai again and then travel to Japan. Her return to her hometown in New York is scheduled for next summer, at which time her travels will have lasted three years. It is said that her next trip will be to China and then to Mongolia, to see the vast scenery.

Announcement of the Auspicious Wedding of Du Yuesheng's Son 143

Increasing Number of Visitors to Yixing's Two Caves 147

The Shanjuan and Gengsang Caves in Yixing are the foremost historical sites in Jiangsu Province. However, due to a lack of artificial management in the past, they have been submerged in obscurity for many years. Recently, thanks to the painstaking efforts of Mr. Chu Nanqiang, a gentleman from Yixing, over the past fifteen years, the caves have been carefully repaired, and their appearance has been completely renewed, gradually attracting the attention of the world. The automobile road now leads directly to the cave entrance, making access much more convenient than in the past. In recent days, visitors have been flocking to the caves in an endless stream, which can be described as a grand event. A reporter, in order to investigate the current situation of the two caves and the transportation conditions, took the special express train from the North Station of Shanghai at 8:00 yesterday morning and arrived in Wuxi at 10:39 (since the 21st of this month, the special express train between Shanghai and Wuxi can be shortened by another 22 minutes). The reporter then hired a car and arrived at Shanjuan Cave at 12:30, finding it deep and magnificent, beyond description. Colorful lanterns are hung throughout the cave, imbuing the solemn atmosphere with a touch of ethereal beauty, instantly giving people a feeling of "a separate world, not of this realm." The floors of each cave have recently been paved with cement, and a deep well, with about a hundred steps, has been dug between the middle and lower caves to facilitate ascending and descending. At the entrance to the lower cave valley, waterfalls and flying springs scatter like beads, making for an extremely pure and secluded environment. The waterways in the rear cave are winding and picturesque, and one can navigate them by boat. After leaving the cave, the reporter crossed the mountain and returned to the front of the Shanjuan Hall, then drove to Gengsang Cave. Inside the cave, countless stalactites hang down like tassels, strangely beautiful and deeply secluded, creating an atmosphere of immense grandeur, befitting the name of an oriental scenic spot. The Shan-Geng Road, which runs from the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway to the two caves, has now been repaved with crushed stone, making it flat, smooth, and extremely sturdy. Even in the event of rain or snow, there is no fear of collapse. The daily progress of transportation in the area is evident from this. Both caves have simple folk restaurants that serve palatable food at low prices, making them especially convenient for travelers. People from Shanghai who go to the caves to see their wonders are coming in droves, mostly taking the 8:00 AM special express train from Shanghai North Station, arriving in Wuxi at 10:17, and then hiring a local car to travel to the two caves for a pleasant visit. They then take the 8:34 PM special express train back to Shanghai on the same day. It is said that if a group of five or six people travel together, the cost can be greatly reduced, with food and transportation costing only about ten yuan per person.

Krupp Isteg Steel Exclusively Managed by Liki Yangxing 148

The well-known German steel factory, Krupp Isteg steel, has a novel and excellent product for steel bars used in reinforced concrete, which has been on the market for a long time, called Krupp Isteg steel bars. Its yield point is at least 50% higher than ordinary mild steel bars, so the safe tensile force used can also be at least 50% higher, while remaining completely safe and without any drawbacks. Therefore, by using Krupp Isteg steel bars, only two-thirds the weight of ordinary mild steel bars is needed, but the price is slightly higher than ordinary mild steel bars. However, because the weight is greatly reduced, costs can be saved by at least 15% to 20%. The amount of Krupp Isteg steel bars used is increasing daily in Europe, and it will surely become popular in China in the future, because no construction company or owner would be unwilling to adopt them in order to save 20% of the cost of steel bars used in reinforced concrete. Krupp Isteg steel bars have been tested and approved by the Shanghai Municipal Council, which acknowledged that their safe tensile force is 50% greater than ordinary mild steel bars. The exclusive agent for Krupp Isteg steel bars in China is Liki Yangxing, located at 220 Sichuan Road in Shanghai. For detailed information about this novel steel bar, please inquire at the Yangxing.

Overview of Narcotics Control in the Public Concession Last Month 161

According to a report from the Public Concession Police Department, in November, the Narcotics Group of the Central Police Station received and searched a total of 22 cases, arresting 84 opium smokers. From the cases reported and searched by various police stations, there were a total of 116 cases, arresting 186 opium smokers. Those convicted were sentenced to imprisonment for 207 people, imprisonment and fines for 17 people, fines only for 121 people, released for 103 people, detained for 17 people, and withdrawn for 2 people. Of the 4 opium smokers detained in October, 2 have been sentenced to imprisonment, and the other 2 have been handed over to the Special Zone No. 2 Court for further investigation. There are still 4 opium smokers who have been detained since the 4th of this year. The narcotics seized include more than 96 taels of opium, more than 641 taels of opium substitutes, less than 1 tael of morphine, more than 3 taels of heroin, 120 opium pipes, and 11 morphine needles. The total amount of fines for these narcotics is 5,780 yuan.

An Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce, Edited by the China Credit Investigation Office, The Cement Industry in Shanghai (Continued) 162

(VII) Productivity

According to investigations, the production capacity of the Shanghai, China, and Qixin factories is 3.1 million barrels of cement per year, including 640,000 barrels in Shanghai, 900,000 barrels in China, and 1.6 million barrels in Qixin. However, judging from the annual output of the above three factories, it is always below its production capacity. The recent three-year output of each factory is listed in the table on the left: (each barrel is equivalent to 170 kg)

As for the output in the past ten months of this year, Shanghai has an average of 5.6 million kilograms per month, China has an average of 8.9 million kilograms per month, and Qixin has an average of 14.5 million kilograms per month; compared with last year, both have decreased. (To be continued)

(VIII) Sales

The sales area of Shanghai Cement Company is mainly in this port, accounting for 70% of the total sales, and large commercial ports such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui account for 30%. The products of China Cement Company are mostly sold in large commercial ports such as Shanghai, Nanjing, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang. Because Qixin Cement Company does not have branches or distributors in major commercial ports across the country, its sales range is wider, almost all over the country. According to investigations, the Shanghai general wholesale office of the company sells about 700,000 barrels to Jiangsu and Fujian each year, mainly in this port; the Tianjin general office sells 500,000 barrels to Hebei, Henan, Shandong, and Shanxi each year; the Hankou general wholesale office sells 200,000 barrels to Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei each year; the Fengtian general wholesale office sells 200,000 barrels to the three northeastern provinces each year, but since the September 18th Incident, the northeast market has been seized, and the North China region has also been affected by the dumping of Japanese goods, and sales have gradually become sluggish.

As for the sales volume this year, the first half of the year was not bad, but since the second half of the year, as the market has become more and more depressed, sales have declined daily, so the sales volume has decreased month by month. According to investigations, Shanghai Cement Company sold an average of 6 million kilograms per month in the first half of the year, and in the past three months, the average may be less than 5 million kilograms. China Cement Company's average monthly sales volume in the first half of the year was 10 million kilograms, and since the second half of the year, the average monthly sales volume has been only 8.9 million kilograms.

(IX) Business Overview

The business situation of Chinese-owned factories was the best in 1932, when the construction industry in this port was booming and the market price was firm and high, with only 6 corners of consolidated tax levied per barrel. Since the end of 1932, the consolidated tax has been changed to 1 yuan and 2 corners per barrel, and the cost has increased. At the same time, imports of foreign goods have increased sharply and prices have been lowered for dumping, and the sales of domestically produced cement have been hindered, and business has declined daily. Until July 1934, the government increased import tariffs (it is estimated that the import tax for every 100 kilograms of cement increased to 8 corners and 3 cents of customs gold), and imports of foreign goods suddenly decreased. The demand for domestically produced cement gradually increased, and the supply was not sufficient. The business of each factory has improved. In the most recent months of this year, due to the depressed market, the business of each factory has also trended downwards.

The market price for cement sales is uniform. The above three factories have jointly organized the Domestic Cement Business Office at 33 Sichuan Road, Shanghai, specializing in cement trading, and have agreed on the market price. Each factory sends staff to be stationed at the office all the time, so that customers can contact them. All wholesale transactions in this port are directly ordered from the business office or the factory, and the payment is settled at that time or paid at the end of the month in installments. As for retail purchases, contact the hardware store. If you want to set up a management office in another port, you can sign a contract with the factory, but you must have a reputable business shop guarantee or pay a certain amount of deposit. The management office handles goods from the company, based on the principle that it does not exceed the deposit paid, and the payment is settled on a monthly basis. All tariffs and transportation costs are borne by the management office; in addition to giving special discounts, the company also rewards with considerable commissions.

(X) Recent Market Price

Recently, due to the cold market and the stagnation of construction, the products of each factory have formed a situation of oversupply, and the market price has frequently trended downwards. According to investigations, the price of the Elephant brand produced in Shanghai was still around 7 yuan per barrel in February of this year (including consolidated tax). Until recently, it has plummeted by more than 1 yuan, and it is now only sold for between 5 yuan and 78 corners.

The price of China's Taishan brand is similar to that of Shanghai, and it has also fallen across the board.

As for the price of Qixin's Horse brand, it is currently sold for about 6 yuan and 6 corners per barrel, including consolidated tax, and each bag is sold for about 2 yuan, both of which are lower than before.

It is said that recently, in view of the rising raw material prices and the interruption of foreign goods sources after the currency system reform, each company has increased the price of cement by 1 yuan and 3 corners per barrel since this month. (The End)

Education News

Shandong Provincial Government Orders Jinan Middle School to Close for Holiday to Prevent the Expansion of the Patriotic Movement 163

(Jinan Correspondence) Students of the provincial senior high school in this city went on strike on the 16th due to the patriotic movement, organized a national salvation group, issued declarations, and told students in the province, and sent representatives to contact other schools in the city, and the schools responded unanimously. Today (17th), Jinan Junior High School and other schools joined the strike. He Siyuan, Director of the Department of Education, convened a meeting of principals of public and private secondary schools in the city at the Department of Education at about 10:00 this morning to discuss solutions. Those who attended the meeting were He Siyuan, Director of the Department of Education, Kong Lingcan, Director of the Secretariat, Liu Cixiao, Secretary, Liu Shuming, President of Qilu University, Yin, President of the Medical College, Song Huanwu, President of the Senior High School, Sun Weiyu, President of Jinan Junior High School, Lu Mengfan, President of Zhengyi Middle School, Qu Taiyi, President of Yuying Middle School, and Zhang Zhuxi of Weicun Middle School. After the meeting, He Siyuan reported and asked the principals to return to school to persuade the students to study at ease. In the afternoon, the students still did not show any signs of resuming classes. The Department of Education convened another meeting of the schools and reported to the provincial government. Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Provincial Government, then discussed with He Siyuan, Director of the Department of Education, that since it was only two weeks before the New Year's holiday, if the students did not resume classes, it would be better to bring the vacation forward by two weeks to avoid the expansion of the incident. The Department of Education then drafted a notice and distributed it to the schools to announce the holiday, and ordered the students living on campus to leave the school and go home.

Middle School Graduates: Academic and Vocational Guidance Testing; Municipal Education Bureau Schedules Event to Begin on the 23rd; Dates and Examiners Assigned 166

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued an order yesterday to municipal and registered private secondary schools in the city, stating, "In order to enhance the effectiveness of academic and vocational guidance for secondary school graduates, the Bureau has decided to send staff to various schools to conduct academic and vocational guidance tests for secondary school graduates before the end of each semester, starting this academic year. This is to observe students' personalities and interests and to develop effective guidance methods. The first semester of the 24th year is about to end. Dr. Wu Dingliang Creates Accurate Age Calculation Tool 174

Chinese people, except for those from Hunan, consider a baby to be one year old at birth and increase their age by one year with each New Year. Therefore, a baby born on New Year's Eve is considered to be two years old on New Year's Day of the following year. This method of calculating age differs from the actual age by as much as one to two years. It is generally considered that this error is not important, but in sciences such as medicine, hygiene, human society, education, and psychology, it is crucial to calculate and study based on the actual age. Therefore, in recent years, many Chinese scientists have been calculating actual age from the nominal age. The various methods used include the following:

(1) Hsu's Sliding Scale and Calculation Table for Actual Age

Professor Hsu Wen-sheng of Peking Union Medical College published a method for calculating actual age using a sliding scale in the Chinese Medical Journal in 1923. The scale is divided into three rows, A, B, and C. A represents the Gregorian calendar month, B represents the lunar calendar month, with the lunar and Gregorian calendars always differing by one month, and C represents the distance in months. A slider is attached to the top, which can be moved left and right to align with the month to be examined. When used, the slider is aligned with row A, which represents the month of measurement. When aligned with row B, it represents the month of birth of the child. Then, the distance between the alignment points of rows A and B is found on row C, and the actual age of the child is calculated from this distance. Four years later, Hsu and Pan created an actual age calculation table based on the previous method and published it in the same journal. The table lists the number of years and months to be subtracted from the nominal age. When calculating, simply look up the intersection of the row for the lunar birth month and the column for the Gregorian calculation month, and subtract the number listed at that intersection from the nominal age to obtain the actual age.

(2) Actual Age Calculation Table Issued by the Ministry of Education

The method for calculating actual age issued by the Ministry of Education on October 10th of the 19th year of the Republic is based on the same principle as the previous table. However, it uses both subtraction and addition. When calculating, simply subtract the number of years to be subtracted from the nominal age, then add the number of months to be added to obtain the actual age. In addition, the actual age calculation method published by Yan Xinzhe and the actual age conversion table printed by the Commercial Press are completely the same as the one issued by the Ministry of Education. Although the above methods are slightly better than calculating actual age using nominal age, they are still not very accurate. Because the calculations are all based on months, in other words, if the birthday and the date of the examination for two people are both in the same month but one is at the beginning and one is at the end of the month, there is no difference on these tables, but in reality, there may be a difference of up to one month. The tables do not list leap years and leap months. Failure to calculate Gregorian leap years results in a difference of only one day. Failure to calculate lunar leap months results in a difference of 29 or 30 days. This type of error seems difficult to ignore. Moreover, none of the tables can be used to calculate the corresponding dates of the Gregorian and lunar calendars, the heavenly stems and earthly branches, or the days of the week.

(3) Hong and Chen's Table of Gregorian and Lunar Calendar Correspondences

Hong published a book in 1910 titled "Correspondence between Gregorian and Lunar Calendar Dates," which contains 569 pages, covering the years from 841 to 2020 of the Gregorian calendar, a total of 1,179 years. The table lists the first day of each lunar month and the corresponding Gregorian date, and also includes the heavenly stems and earthly branches for each month and the first day of each day. To find the correspondence for any date, it is necessary to calculate day by day from the first day of each day. Chen's "Chinese-Western-Islamic Calendar" was published in 1926, in five volumes, covering the years from the Gregorian era (the first year of Emperor Ping of Han) to 1940 (the 29th year of the Republic of China). It was created by calculating the correspondences between the three calendars day by day using mechanical methods. The last volume also includes tables of heavenly stems and earthly branches, days of the week, etc. The tables created by the above two individuals are both based on days and include leap years and leap months, making them very accurate. However, because the volumes are numerous, checking them takes a lot of time, and it is extremely difficult to calculate the distance between two different periods from them. The price of the books is relatively high, and they are not affordable for the average person.

(4) Actual Age Calculation Tool

Recently created by Dr. Wu Dingliang of the Academia Sinica, it only requires knowing a person's nominal age and the month and day of their lunar birth to instantly calculate: 1. A person's Gregorian and lunar birth year; 2. A person's Gregorian birth month and day; 3. The heavenly stems and earthly branches of a person's birth year, month, and day; 4. The day of the week of a person's birth; 5. The distance between a person's birth date and the date of the examination, i.e., a person's actual age. The above methods can not only be applied to modern people, but also to the conversion of the lunar and Gregorian dates of historical figures' chronologies and historical facts. Its advantages include at least the following: Accurate calculation: The tool is based on days, and includes Gregorian leap years and lunar leap months, with no error. Time-saving: It takes no more than 40 seconds to find the above five answers, which is faster than specifically finding the corresponding dates of the Gregorian and lunar calendars in the books of Hong and Chen. Convenient to use: The tool is made of wood, with three outer, middle, and inner wheels. Each wheel is engraved with various degrees. The outer and inner wheels are fixed. When used, only the middle wheel needs to be moved, and the various answers can be obtained in order. It resembles a compass, is 6 inches in diameter and 8 points thick, making it easy to carry. Detailed instructions are provided separately. It is anticipated that the invention of this tool will be beneficial to the educational community.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men 189

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Mrs. March paused at the foot of the stairs, looking quite weary after her fright and the long journey.

"Poor Aunt March is so tired, she needs someone to help her upstairs herself," gentle Franz said, as he put his arm around her.

"Let's make a big armchair for her," Tommy suggested.

"No, thank you, my boys; but if someone would lend me a shoulder to lean on, that would do," Mrs. March replied.

"Me! Me!" five or six voices exclaimed at once, for there was something in that pale, motherly face that touched the hearts under those round jackets.

Mrs. March, seeing that they regarded it as an honor, gave it to the most deserving one, so there was not a murmur when she leaned on Don's broad shoulder, and the grateful look on her face made his cheek flush with pleasure, as she said:

"He found the children; so I think he must help me up."

Don felt that he had been richly rewarded for his work that evening, and not only did he proudly carry the lamp and escort Mrs. March upstairs, but as he was about to leave her at her door, she said sincerely, "Good-night, my boy! God bless you!"

"I wish I really was your boy!" said Don, feeling as if hardship and tribulation had brought him nearer to her.

"You may be my big boy," she said, as she sealed the deep feeling with a touch of her hand.

Finance: Speculation Exceeds Limits for the First Time, Silver Prices Plummet Limitlessly, Foreign Exchange Can Still Be Maintained in the Short Term, People's Concern Lies Here 190

Yesterday, the gold market suddenly experienced a surge. The central bank initially opened with strong buying interest. Later, after a large transaction, the price fell to 19.5 pence, and various rumors about currency systems spread. By closing, the price had risen to around 76 yuan. In the morning, news came from overseas stating that large forward transactions were still halted, with the base reporting no transactions from the US. Large transactions could not be completed, with recent listings at 23 pence, which was the seller's price, down 1.875 pence from the previous day. American silver fell by 3 cents, and forward silver prices in Monte Video fell by 1 to 2 cents, etc. The exchange rate was stable. The price of gold in London rose by 1.5 pence, and reports indicated some gold exports, boosting confidence. The central bank's listed exchange rates for British and American currencies remained stable, while the customs gold unit rose by 4%. The standard gold price listed rose to 1148.6 yuan. Pre-market trading opened at around 48 yuan. Fuxing, Yongda, and Decheng all advanced. The morning opened with high prices, once breaking through the 50 yuan mark. Foreign banks seized the opportunity to sell, and the exchange rate gradually stabilized. Sellers took advantage of the high prices to become active, gradually lowering prices. Major players still had strong selling intentions, falling to 47.6 yuan. HSBC's listed rates for British and American currencies were stable, keeping people calm. After the fall, prices gradually stabilized and fluctuated. When the silver equalization tax was announced, falling by 10.5%, it had no impact. Buyers became more active and rebounded. Rumors spread that the central bank was buying 390+ bars of spot silver, boosting confidence and breaking through the 50 yuan mark again. Despite major players seizing the opportunity to sell at high prices, the market was optimistic, and buying interest surged. At noon, prices continued to rise, and the same was true after closing. This was because a certain foreign firm's private cable reported that large transactions had fallen to 19.5 pence after closing. The market became more confident, continuing to rise. However, due to the strength of the three major banks in suppressing short-term foreign exchange, prices fluctuated around 60 yuan. Despite repeated attempts by Chinese and foreign banks to intervene, forward foreign exchange remained tight, buying interest surged, and rumors abounded. Major players competed to buy, rising again to around 70 yuan. Subsequently, prices fell back slightly due to the entry and exit of major players. However, the market's eagerness remained strong, and buyers rushed in one after another. Short positions were caught off guard and rushed to cover, breaking through the 70 yuan mark. The closing price rose as high as 76 yuan, and swaps also rose, with shorts paying 9.5 yuan. The market changed dramatically in one day. Would industry players regain their momentum? The future of the gold market is difficult to predict. Here is a record of the day's market conditions:

The morning opening was at 1147 yuan, up 2 yuan from the previous closing. Fuxing, Yongchun, Yuanyong, Hui Xiang, Dafa, and Yong all rose to 50.38 yuan, 50.5 yuan and 50.75 yuan. Chunyuan, Yongzhen, Tai, Richang, Hengchang, and Yong took advantage of the low prices to make purchases, rising to 50.93 yuan. Citibank released February American dollars at 25.
