In the Wind and Snow 205

— Zigang

There is no killing, no fighting, but people's hearts have become as dark as the weather. From which gust of wind did this bloodless smell come?

Darkness not only surrounds people's hearts, but also envelops the earth. People are trapped in dreams, not knowing what kind of days they are living. Unparalleled chaos is in front of their eyes, and their throats are suffocating as if something is stuck in them. Their feet are like a ship that has hit a reef, tossing and sinking. What is most certain is that this ferocious storm will end your cries. In this instant, the emotion that covers your heart is anger—anger covers fear—open your eyes wide and look into the distance, but it is too late to resent and ask for help.

"Iron crows, one, two, three..."

"Red dots—"

People shielded their foreheads with their hands and looked at the sky. The sky was filled with green clouds.

Old women began to scold: "Why doesn't the wind blow them down?" Children, however, instinctively picked up stones in their hands and threw them into the air, pouting: "Beat you to death!"

The voices of newspaper sellers on the streets and alleys were even more lively. "News" expanded its territory in people's hearts. People did not forget to prick up their ears to listen. In the dead of night, mixed with the cries of hawkers, the voices of newspaper boys touched people's heartstrings. Everyone had their own plans, but the overall implication was: a very important eve had arrived. The newspaper boys on the carts added new lyrics to their calls, almost using the same attitude as distributing pamphlets to attract customers. Their efforts were not in vain. Many hands did not hesitate to spend that big coin.

The advertising columns were filled with advertisements for "× Language Crash Courses," specifying "× Overseas Chinese" or "Studied × Abroad." Apart from the tactics, the consistency was: speculation, making a living.

On the streets and in the markets, there were more sounds of wooden clogs and beards with *Jintan* toothpaste powder on them. Women with heavy makeup carried small leather balls on the streets, and they still had to hold up their vests when sitting in rickshaws. The small leather balls chattered behind their backs, as if they were endlessly puzzled by this new place. Who can explain the magic of this ancient city?

Small bicycles were constantly coming and going in the alleys near ×× Elementary School. Children with mailbox-like schoolbags on their backs were pedaling hard, giggling and sliding past. Children playing with piles of gray sand on the ground squinted and muttered after calculating for a while:

"Little ××, selling cold noodles... (Note: a nursery rhyme.)

The signs of foreign companies were hung densely, so many that they were inexplicable, but the open secret was only chilling. Suddenly, they remembered some people in the Northeast who had lost their fortunes, those thin skeletons with sunken eyes were shaking in front of them.

When they heard the not-so-low sound of gunfire, people immediately gained wisdom after being frightened: it was ×× soldiers practicing shooting. On the ×× parade ground on the street, clusters of soldiers in uniforms with red edges gathered, short, smoky legs running on the sandy ground. Others were riding horses. People walked by quietly, muttering some spells in their hearts and starting some unrealistic dreams.

But dreams are just dreams.

When newspapers, like electric currents, only brought disappointment when they touched their eyes, people sighed deeply. Although some old diehards were still walking on the sidewalks with their birdcages covered with cotton covers, with the mentality of letting it go. Merchants frowned for the dark clouds. The station was abnormally crowded. The scales at the baggage room door and the boxes and cages were piled up like mountains. Cowardly souls bid farewell to this ancient city for the last time, harboring a little sorrow for it.

The Dongjiaominxiang (Legation Quarter) added more vehicles and horses. Some fat-headed and big-eared people found a sheltered place again, as if a child had entered its mother's arms.

Young people couldn't bear this suffocation and roared like lions, making righteous calls. The common people saw the cloud-like troops and inquired with each other. Flowers bloomed on their worried faces, joy floated in their hearts, and a little hope and a little light grew.

Swords and gun stocks appeared. More compatriots with belts were added to the roadblocks, listening to commands and doing things that they themselves did not understand, and a pleading expression was implied in the expulsion. The fire truck's faucet emitted water, acting as a fire extinguisher to extinguish the flames, but it was sweeping people. Young people retreated in the water flow and gun stocks, leaving a street of ice.

In the north wind, the coolies did not forget these interesting (?) dramas, discussing and regretting. The wind and clouds of the North Country flashed in people's hearts.

Dream of Snow 206

— Heiding

It is another cold and gloomy winter.

Yet there is still no snow. For days, all the shadows under the sun have been pushed into the dark crevices of the earth by a layer of dim color. My room is filled with dim light, and it is cold. In this way, loneliness gives me some sad and long feelings. I am used to poking my head out of the window, with a thoughtful expression, staring with bright eyes, blankly, at the light and thin floating clouds scattered in the ancient and quiet sky. Concentrating.

Is it going to snow?

I took a deep breath. I have a string of silent shouts. My mood is suffering from the winter seasonal disease. My thoughts are disturbed by the dream of snow.

I disinterestedly shrunk my head back, and the window closed easily. I paced around the room.

Remembering—

A long, long time ago, I sadly wrote this small essay:

A dog in the snow thinks of home.

Wavelike heart, no way to arrange. Melancholy eyes, staring at the snowflakes outside the window, flying down one by one.

Life is like a snowflake flying to the ground.

Wandering dream, lost the road of youth, lonely trudging on this dark road of life

It has been more than two years since I went home.

It is now deep winter, my body is sadly cold, and my heart is sadly cold! I just think: the snow in my hometown should be falling in large swaths, covering the entire earth with white.

I love the snow in my hometown, the snow in my hometown hides the spring of my childhood.

However, the snow in my hometown is now stained with bright red blood! Shouldn't we lightly forget that lost free home!

It must be said to be a sad thing, since the great uprising of September 18th, my home was broken, and my family members were exiled, so I slowly forgot my home! Then I began to take the strength of life and step firmly on the road to wandering.

The heart is ardent, and it is also looking forward to the light of the future.

Sometimes, the heart is smiling and caningly whispering: Quickly follow the wheels of history and turn to a new stage.

So, I was reborn.

I have no home. I wander everywhere. I identify a direction.

I have tasted a lot of the bitterness of life alone; this journey of life, how long and fast it is!

Often a little small stimulus will slow down my forward force, which is my biggest shortcoming. However, I can always remember that people have to move forward to be able to live.

I have already forged myself into a person who is used to living in a foreign land. But at the same time, I have also become a melancholy person; I did not smile in spring, I did not smile in summer, I did not smile in autumn, and in winter, I looked at the snowflakes outside the window and added a touch of sadness!

Now, the winter in ××, where I am staying, is deep, and my heart is also heavily ill! I can't help but sing a dirge to this first snow

So, I thought of home.

The deep winter in the Northeast, what a beautiful world of snow it should be!

Can I still open my throat and shout out the sad melody of my heart?

A lonely wanderer who has lost his home spends a long and desolate life in sour and eternal, which is really a kind of unbearable bitterness! This mood is like a black net, tightly covering my entire mind, but it makes me suffocate without a breath. I have no day, night is my narrow world. The wings of sorrow cannot leave my surroundings. I curse the day, and I curse the night. I don't know what will excite me and make me laugh foolishly. But I also don't know what will excite me and make me cry timidly. At night, I have become accustomed to not sleeping even once, and I love to wander alone in the dead streets illuminated by the stars. I feel that this is my happiest moment. I have been careful to count the days since I was a child, and even on my birthday, I let it pass secretly. My mood is getting older day by day. In autumn and winter, when a leaf falls on my body, I blankly shudder! But I am not surprised, I stand down calmly. I know that the change of seasons is turning again under my feet. Therefore, I want to shout loudly for a while. But my shout is dumb. My side is so lonely, I can't see a person's shadow. (There is a large pile of skeletons, let it go, it will eventually be destroyed!) I began to think that I was indeed too lonely, I needed friends, and I needed fresh air even more.

But the night air formed a ball of hazy mist.

I walk carefully. I'm afraid of falling. But my roadside has two very deep mud ditches.

In this way, after a year, two years,... sorrow no longer belongs to me. Home, home, the home that gave birth to me, I simply dare not put it in my thoughts anymore. I'm afraid it will provoke me and make me restless on the road. What a worm that is easy to stimulate my troubles.

Home, home, the shadow of home gradually diminished in my thoughts.

Even in winter, I no longer think of home.

(The snow in my hometown emits a white light in my dream)

On the road where there are homes for wanderers everywhere, I have seen all the same seasons pass before my eyes. For example, the winter in the south is not easy to see snowy days. This is a disturbing thing. But the winter in the north is not like that, the cold has changed to another face, the ground is covered with snowflakes, but the mountains and fields are covered with white.

I have never stopped my walking because of the snow, and I feel very happy on the road. I often shout wildly to the mountains and fields. I also often chant softly to the snow. Snow is no longer familiar in my inspiration. It is my faithful travel companion. I have never cursed it, I think it is lovely. Always, it is sometimes wrapped by the violent northwest wind and pounced on my face, but I run quickly, and in no time, my body will be immersed in sweat. My face is steaming, and the snowflakes gradually turn into water. I walk, I listen to the snow scratching under my feet. The sound is really fresh.

But sometimes, I have also been blown by the snow, and I have been sick several times in a mountain village home. It's okay, I still wouldn't curse it. It is lovely. It is my faithful travel companion.

Braving the snow, I have been to many small towns. Therefore, I met several young friends who were of the same mind.

On the banks of the cold Erguna River, there are shadows of several of our young friends every day. The snow on the banks of the river is deeply stepped on by the footprints of our vagrants.

However, unexpectedly, those young friends of mine were finally swallowed up by the dark evil forces. Leaving me, lonely, still a wanderer.

Now, winter has come. Shouldn't the winter scenery of the northern wilderness be a white sheet again?

So, my thoughts are disturbed by the dream of snow.

My past hard life on the snowy ground. My past few young friends who were killed.

Ancient Capital 207

— Fanhai

Barren land cannot grow lush flowers,

What irrigates our ancient capital is

The dust rolled in from beyond the Great Wall, and ××'s greed;

Ancient palace-style low houses are like rat holes,

The streets are full of cries of slaughter,

The rich anesthetize themselves with opium,

The grandmothers are yellow-faced, which of the mothers of the motherland is not a mummy in the Egyptian pyramid?

Which place is not as poor as a beggar?

The cold wind outside the Great Wall is howling,

You twisting Miss, oh,

There are too few of you, one or two can't be seen on the street, so few,

Why dress so well in this ancient city,

Like adding flowers to a skull;

Why make tempting gestures,

Like dancing in a graveyard!

Who guarantees that the city under this ancient capital will not be a battlefield for contention tomorrow?

Who guarantees that sparks will not burst out from underground tomorrow?

Humanity and Immortals 208

— Leng Mo

Writers of the old Russian era often used love stories to express their political views. Although they achieved considerable success in the literary realm of storytelling, making readers feel they were experiencing pure art without perceiving any political undertones, readers often understood and sympathized with the authors' hidden intentions. In Chinese literary works, a portion of untitled poems can be said to have been created using a similar technique, but their attitude is often not very serious, so what they can express is not a definitive opinion, but only some delicate techniques. By the time readers see them, the author's original intention cannot be noticed. Perhaps the author did not fail to hope to make a deeper expression, but the environment limited him. To use the view of love to express the view of politics, it is first necessary to be able to express their view of love as much as possible, but talking about love in old China, just like talking about politics in old Russia, could become a crime. Therefore, what is similar to using love to symbolize politics is not those allegorical untitled poems, but rather those stories that use immortals and ghosts to express human love. Hereafter, these are collectively referred to as Immortal-Ghost stories. Perhaps because the habit of banning talk of love in China was too deep, the reason why the author had to describe it that way seems to have never been noticed. Now, the narration of immortal-ghost stories seems to have become the most ridiculed point of old-fashioned literati, which is really a bit unfair. Generally, suppressed emotions will erupt in strange ways, and the narration of immortal-ghost stories sometimes cannot be denied as a way for old-time literati to express their suppressed emotions. The stimulation of suppressed emotions is often the cause of great works, although immortal-ghost stories have not produced many works that have reached as good as expected, but it is not necessarily that they should all be dismissed.

Comparing modern fox-ghost stories with Tang Dynasty legends, one can generally lament the decline of works. Looking at the content, we can see that they become more and more absurd, but we must not forget that part of the reason is due to the tighter and tighter shackles. From "The Story of Yingying," which can be circulated, we know that the people of the Tang Dynasty did have considerable tolerance for love, but later generations have a lot of discussion about this article, because the story is about Zhang Sheng, inferring that the protagonist is Zhang Ji, then criticizing Zhang Ji, and some infer that it is the author's self-narration, then criticizing Yuan Zhen. Later generations of authors, seeing such encounters, naturally dare not repeat the same mistake and leave discussions for later generations, not to mention that perhaps criticism does not have to wait for later generations, and contemporary people will come to criticize. The Tang Dynasty's legends of immortal encounters are probably not fabricated, but conceal actual human events, just like Li Shangyin's untitled poems, the facts contained in them, if they were clearly stated at the time, would be enough to bring disaster, so they could not pretend to encounter immortals. Zhang Zhu's "Youxian Cave" probably records what he encountered was a proud, extravagant, and lewd princess. Shen Yazhi's "Jin Ci Ji" even hopes to see ancient empresses, which may not be said to involve the palace. If it can be inferred in this way, then the ingenious technique of concealing real events with the guise of bizarre faces has achieved considerable results. It is only natural that later generations specialized in following this ingenious technique.

The legendary aspects were inherited by later notes, and on the one hand, they also developed into popular novels. Novels in the style of talented scholars and beautiful women can also be said to be a main vein of legends. This aspect seems to focus on the human world, but as soon as we see the uniformity of the stories in these novels, we immediately feel that the human world that is allowed to be written is really pitifully small. No matter how low the author's talent is, it is difficult for us to assume that he does not even have the slightest ambition to try to escape the prison. The author really does not want to escape, but is not allowed to escape. The author of "Hua Jian Ji," at the beginning, explained his idea: "As long as both parties can complete the relationship, then what harm is there in secretly dating?" This limit of complete relationship is almost maintained by the entire society with all its strength, so talented scholars and beautiful women books have to always be so pitiful. An author who wants to write about a wider human world has to entrust it to immortals and ghosts.

Of course, we cannot say that all immortal-ghost stories have their human background. Taoist thought has a long-standing basis and continuous spread in China, and the atmosphere of liking vague and absurd theories is very prevalent, and naturally it will produce many fabricated absurd stories. But we can also say that Taoist imagination can continuously run parallel with Confucian thought, because it has a human basis. Because Taoism is constantly rejected by Confucianism, the ideal world it constructs is only placed in heaven. Originally, Taoism did not fail to want to create such a world in the human world. If Taoist thought had ever occupied the same power as Confucian thought, then the fictional stories could probably also use the human world as the background. The modern life situation after drastic changes, when heard by the old-fashioned people in the countryside, while adhering to Confucian doctrines, they naturally sigh and shake their heads, but sometimes they also feel like listening to beautiful myths, which is enough to illustrate how suppressed emotions want to be expressed.

Once this suppressed emotion is liberated, then immortal-ghost stories will naturally disappear. This can be seen from the gradual decline of "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio" style notes after the rise of erotic novels. "The Directory of Famous Courtesans," which is considered the earliest work of eroticism, allows it to show such a trend. Some people say that the protagonist Qin Yan in the book does not look like a male at all, which is the weakness of this book. But we don't seem to have to regard this book as a realistic depiction of the situation of befriending actors. Its writing method can be said to be still a kind of entrustment, so what is written will naturally not look like a woman. This book is not entirely the same as the later novels about prostitutes. The depiction of prostitutes, due to the limitations of real objects, although the author tries his best to make them faint, often cannot get his wish, so in the end they form like "Nine-tailed Turtle." This is walking out of a narrow human world and walking into another narrow human world. This aspect is no longer enough to express suppressed emotions, and the times have changed. Readers have long had translated romance novels to read, and authors dare to imitate Western works and write romance novels. The wide sales of "The Jade Pear Spirit" are said to be due to the style of the Mandarin Ducks and Butterflies School, but it is not as good as saying that it is due to the ability to appeal to the emotions of ordinary people seeking liberation. At this time, it is possible for real human beings to replace fictional immortals and ghosts. According to reason, real people should be depicted as more active than immortals and ghosts, and the emotional expression in the works should be more beautiful. But up to now, we don't seem to be able to find many moving shadows in new works that exceed what is written in immortal-ghost stories. Great achievements in literature are very difficult to achieve, then immortal-ghost stories are not the least accomplished item in literary works, and to think that it is the most despicable.

Fatalist 209

— Hei Ying

The watchman in our Nanyang newspaper office is not an Indian Asam with a thick beard, but a Shantou man who is getting old quickly, his hair turned white before he was fifty, and his appearance is a bit hunched, which is very strange to me. On the second day I came here to be a small editor, because the manager was a relative, I said to him in a conversation:

"Isn't the Indian Asam more qualified to be a doorman? Our doorman is not majestic enough!"

The person who heard me laughed: "Isn't it? I say you are too young to be the editor-in-chief. Your job now is to find a way to make the newspaper's end better, that's your job. Why do you want to express your opinion to the doorman?"

"Really, I don't like him very much..." I mumbled and walked out of the manager's office.

This hunched old man is called Tang Bing. Not only is his hair white, but he has also lost a few teeth, and his face is wrinkled and ugly. During the day, he sits at the gate, looking at everyone who comes in with dull eyes, without saying a word. We are an afternoon newspaper, so it is especially crowded at noon. Some newspaper delivery guys also enter and exit through the gate, so it is noisy and chaotic, and Tang Bing has absolutely no way to maintain order. He is afraid of people, and occasionally he shouts at a newspaper delivery person who does not keep order in a low voice:

"Don't shout, don't..."

"What are you saying, old thing?"

When that person turned around and faced him with a fierce look, as if he had encountered some great oppression, Tang Bing immediately fell silent and dared not interfere with them anymore.

Such a useless watchman...

My job was not troublesome at all, and I had a lot of free time to sit in the editorial office and read newspapers and magazines sent from various places. Maybe it was because the manager often came here and saw me idle there. One day, he called me over and asked me to sit on the sofa next to the desk in a very kind manner. Then, smoking a cigar, he said to me:

"Our newspaper office is going to be three years old in two months. I want you to do something... like a special issue..."

"Okay. But I..."

"They are all busy," he interrupted me like this. "I see there is still so much time, so you can take it up. It will also be good for you to forge yourself."

In this way, I had to be responsible for the anniversary issue of more than two hundred pages. The newspaper office here does not give manuscript fees as a rule, and I have no way to find someone to write articles. I think it should be my busiest time in these two months.

The days to publication were getting closer and closer, and under the manager's constant urging, I decided to work overtime. So almost every night, in order to have the convenience of consulting books, I went to the newspaper office to work. There, I had more opportunities to get close to Tang Bing.

"Mr. Chen, you're working hard." He sparsely walked into the door of the editorial office, saying this to me.

"Um..." I felt that he had barged in and simply disrupted my thoughts. After responding, I was about to raise my head and tell him to go out, but I saw him under the electric light, smiling kindly, holding a cup of tea in his hand, trembling slightly, and putting it on the table.

"If you want tea, Mr. Chen, just call me." He said.

I nodded. Yes, sometimes when I was thirsty and wanted water, I didn't know who to call. There was no one in the newspaper office! The watchman Tang Bing was naturally always there, and he slept by the door at night with a thin blanket on his body. But I never used him.

"It's cold outside, right?" I saw him still standing there, so I asked casually.

"It's okay. Isn't Mr. Chen also very lonely here alone?"

"If you talk about loneliness, you must be even more so, Tang Bing!" I simply put down my pen and chatted with him.

Tang Bing smiled bitterly: "What can we do? Fate is destined. Mr. Chen, if my son hadn't died, then the situation wouldn't be like this..." As if his sadness was aroused, he stopped talking in a frustrated manner.

I thought, let Tang Bing have a chance to pour out the accumulated depression in his heart. So I asked about his life. He immediately sat down and said to me as if he had found a confidant:

"Mr. Chen, everything is destined by fate. I once had a son. To be honest, this little thing was not bad at all. He studied very hard... I had long wanted to rely on my son in old age. Enjoying the happiness of children and grandchildren is the happiest thing in life, so when his mother died, I was not very sad; I wholeheartedly cultivated him... One day I went to the temple to ask for a lottery, saying that if I didn't cultivate well, I wouldn't be able to enjoy the happiness of children and grandchildren; Mr. Chen, where am I not cultivating with good intentions? It's just that I only have thirty yuan a month, and I have to provide for my son's tuition. At that time, I was a carpenter."

"Then your son..."

"The sacred lottery was fulfilled, I don't have this kind of blessing. My son died of typhoid fever when he was nineteen years old!"

"Oh!" I responded, leaned my back against the back of the chair, and saw a beam of tears that could not flow out from Tang Bing's sluggish eye sockets.

I looked at this old man with sympathetic eyes, but I couldn't say anything after all. He believes in gods, believes in fate; he lacks the ability to recognize reality. In the end, I asked:

"Did you send him to the hospital at that time?"

"Mr. Chen, we are poor people, we can't go to the hospital, so..."

It's eleven o'clock. He should go outside to lock the door and sleep under it, so that he can get twenty yuan in salary. But when he left, he kept murmuring:

"What can you do if fate is destined?"

Not long after, the old watchman was sick. And it was a hopeless disease. The manager sent him to a public hospital. When I went to visit him, he was very concerned about whether the third anniversary issue had been published; asking if I was still going to the newspaper office at night. I felt that he had lost so much weight that only his bones were left...

A few days later, Tang Bing died...

The watchman was replaced by the Indian Asam, tall and majestic. Every time I walked into that gate, he would salute me, his posture was a bit funny. But I often think of the hunched and weak Tang Bing until I returned to China.

Reality of Love 210

— Long Gonggong

Love between the sexes, between parents and children, is sometimes expressed in a strangely abnormal manner — in direct violation of ordinary behavior.

Once, in a filthy, dimly lit little house blackened by coal smoke on Yuanyuan Street in the provincial capital, I ran into a woman. The landlord, Zhu Juexian, was a friend of mine, a fortune teller who made a living by deception. After five months of unemployment, I moved in with him because I had nowhere to live.

She was a nineteen-year-old mother who worked at a medicinal herb shop every day. Her husband worked as a handyman at a tin shop, and together they could earn fourteen yuan a month. Their boy was called A Yu, just two years old, intelligent and strong.

The 1930s—we have a barbaric, violent, cruel world where shameless force is praised or celebrated, and curses and lies are what we hear; this is the truth, and we prove it with any character in any street corner. In fact, the woman I met had a painful life after marriage. She spoke publicly in front of many people about what had happened, from her hometown to Zengcheng, where they spent their "honeymoon," in great detail, concluding with her grievances. Like a lower animal, she was abused by poverty and her own man; like a lower animal, she abused her own child.

Whenever she innocently beat the child, who could not yet speak complete sentences, her neighbors, Mrs. Luo Si, Auntie Yu Gen, the shoemaker Chen Man, and the well digger Bi Tong, would come in and surround her, trying to persuade her with all sorts of words.

"What do you know? What do you know!" she would curse brazenly. "He's my own flesh and blood, and you want to interfere even if I hit him a few times! ... This yellow pest is not just here to collect debts, but to take my life. How would you understand?"

"Be careful, you're going to beat him to death," the well digger Bi Tong roared. "We won't allow it! —You're worse than a bitch!"

"Come on, whoever dares to lay a hand on me, come on!"

If she provoked her husband with these same words, that fiery man would teach her a lesson with his fists, "love" her, and heavily pound her back and chest, without saying a word to her. She would run out into the street, sit on the ground and shout for help, spitting out bright red blood from her mouth.

"Tell me my fortune," she once asked my friend Zhu Juexian.

"Women don't need to have their fortune told!" the fortune teller refused. "Your husband's fortune is your fortune."

Worse Than a Dog 211

— Meng Ruo

Another hotel has been established in Shanghai, but this hotel is not a hotel for people to have a drink, but a dog hotel for dogs to stay and eat. According to reports: Although the Shanghai Ge Road Hunting Dog School charges 50 yuan per month, there are still many hunting dogs being trained. In order to expand the scope, the owner of the school has recently opened a dog hotel, providing two meals a day, mainly beef, and charging 18 yuan per month for food. However, the school's hunting dogs have a monthly fee of 50 yuan, including food and accommodation, so there is no need to pay extra. Because the dog hotel is quite convenient, many Chinese and Western dog owners in the city have been taking their beloved dogs to the hotel to eat, which is very lively.

It is common to see wealthy people who keep dogs treat them with great care, regarding them as sons and daughters. They eat beef, sit in cars, and some even sleep with them in bed at night. Now this dog hotel is opened to meet this need. It is said that dog hotels are very common in major cities in Europe and the United States. The daily fee is very high, often more expensive than the meals of the working class. But the prosperity of the business is no less than that of human hotels. The one established on Haige Road is still an unprecedented initiative in China. In the future, it will be much more convenient for those who keep dogs at home. This is really the happiness of dogs!

But just when we were celebrating for the dogs, we heard the news of a family working together to rob food and clothing, which was very disappointing. This incident happened in various places in the Nanshi Old City. A group of poor people with bird-like faces gathered dozens of people into a group and grabbed steamed buns, pancakes, and other things from dim sum shops along the way to fill their stomachs. None were spared. Occasionally, when the police arrived, the food had already entered their stomachs, and the shop owner could only cry out in vain. There was also a certain tailor who hired a rickshaw the other day to load 300 sets of finished cotton trousers, intending to transport them to a foreign goods store for delivery. Unexpectedly, after passing Xiaobeimen, a group of ragged people rushed forward and robbed six cotton trousers. By the time the police arrived, they had already escaped without a trace. This is the misfortune of human beings!

As far as we know, a catered meal in Shanghai only costs six or seven yuan per month per person. Sending an infant to a nursery also only costs twelve yuan per person per month. Now this dog hotel provides two meals a day, and the daily fee is eighteen yuan, which is much higher than the living standard of people. Moreover, dogs have the good fortune to enter hotels, but people need to risk robbery to get food and clothing! In comparison, how can one not sigh: It's worse than a dog!

However, the people mentioned here refer to the poor, which is not the case for the rich. For example, recently the thermometer has gradually dropped, and some poor people who have no food and clothing have already starved to death and frozen to death! Another part of the rich are eating bird's nest and cod liver oil in warm, spring-like rooms, waiting to watch the snow! "Behind the vermilion gates, meat and wine are left to rot, while on the road lie the bones of those who have frozen to death." These two sentences are the best portrayal of this phenomenon!

Snow 212

— Hua Mu

Although Shanghai is said to be a place in Jiangnan, it is not as good as the Lingbiao area in the south. There is no snow in winter. Wouldn't its face be so dry that people feel uncomfortable? In winter over there, although you can hear the howling north wind sweeping past outside the window, you can also see the green and yellow leaves of the trees. You can think of it as autumn in Jiangnan to comfort yourself, but when you look up and see the color of the clouds painted on the corner of the building, it will make the bright autumn feeling in your heart disappear.

Now you can rest assured, you don't have to worry about it anymore. When will the snow fall? It would be embarrassing to say it out loud. Of course, if you live in the north, this thought would not have to be hanging in your throat until now. It has long snowed in the north, and some rivers and seas have even frozen, and boats cannot travel. What you see and feel is just the freezing and cold all over the sky! Isn't that kind of scene the face of winter? Shanghai belongs to the southern region after all, so winter naturally comes later; however, in the past few days, hasn't the mercury on the Celsius thermometer dropped to twenty degrees or so? Look at the sky without the sun, the accumulated frozen clouds, snowfall will not be delayed beyond two days. As long as it rains tonight or tomorrow morning, you can see snowflakes flying all over the sky, and then cover the earth in a white expanse! At that time, several inches of snow will pile up thickly on the steps of your home, making you love it and unwilling to step on its whiteness with muddy shoes and spoil it. You should be satisfied and happy, you are surprised, you jump for joy, wishing you could also differentiate into white snowflakes, flying in the sky, floating in the sky, and then quietly covering the branches and grass; when the sun comes, it will reflect dazzling light, beauty does not lack solemnity. Then it will gently dissolve into droplets of water, moisturizing the seeds of flowers and plants buried underground. Isn't such a dream gorgeous and splendid enough?

However, you also have to find a way to dissipate and grind away this beautiful snowy day. Snowball fights and snowmen are all things that children play with, and you may not feel interested. Treading through the snow to find plum blossoms is a bit too elegant, and you also have to be able to find plum blossoms nearby. Shanghai has asphalt roads, and there are no mountains to speak of. Even if you can't find plum blossoms in the garden of the mansion, but not everyone may have a garden like the Grand View Garden. People in the garden can only look over the wall (maybe you can't even see it). Of course, if you are interested, it is not impossible to take the train to Dengwei, Suzhou. No one will interfere with you in such a bad mood. It's just that this way of playing is not something that everyone can do. Then how about seeking the next best thing? You always have friends. When it snows, you may wish to send a small invitation to invite them to come, roast by the fire, warm the pot with hot wine, and everyone have a round-the-stove meeting to talk about the past and present of the world, but you don't have to force people to write poetry. This is the cliché of celebrities and can be left to them. It's a pity that you can't buy venison in Shanghai, otherwise you can also imitate the story of Shi Xiangyun and Jia Baoyu roasting venison alive at the Luxue Pavilion. The taste is guaranteed to be rich, fragrant, and wild!

You have muddled through the daytime, maybe you are tired. Naturally, you won't think about going out at night. If you go to bed too early, you may not be able to fall asleep on the bed (if you have a wife, naturally it's up to you at this time, excuse me, I don't have a wife yet, I can't say this taste). At this time, it is best to learn from the ancients, the joy of "reading banned books behind closed doors on a snowy night." That kind of fun can only be felt by you personally, and words are difficult to describe. The scope of banned books mentioned here is very broad, and it does not necessarily refer to obscene books. You think there is wind and snow outside, who else will come to be an uninvited guest and knock on your door at this late hour? You can read to your heart's content and have a great time. Is there anything happier in life than this?

In short, snow can make you happy, make you happy, make you forget the cold, and give you a gorgeous and splendid dream. I don't want you to be a celebrity or an elegant person. It doesn't matter if you are as unrestrained as possible when you are bold. But don't be pretentious.

Wait, the snow will always fall.

The Old Man Who Traps Coots 213

— Xinye

After three consecutive nights of northwesterly winds, the weather has become quite cold. The old mulberry trees, which still had some remaining leaves a month ago, are now bare, revealing a landscape of deathly grey, devoid of any vitality from nature.

Ye Ya San (Wild Duck Three) turned over in bed and saw a faint light seeping through the cracks in the tiles. He jumped out of bed, draped himself in an old cotton-padded coat as old as he was, and reached out to push open the wooden window. A sharp gust of cold wind rushed in, causing him to shrink his neck into his collar and instinctively shiver! He walked out of the room, hung a tobacco basket on his arm, shouldered his oar in the doorway, closed the broken white wooden doors through which wild dogs could squeeze in and out, and locked the rusty iron ring. He crossed the small bridge, pulled his rolled-brim felt hat down tightly, tightened his waist, braved the biting wind, and headed towards the riverbank.

The wind swirled powerfully in the air, causing the bare tree trunks to bow repeatedly. A thick layer of frost covered the withered grass, as white as if it had snowed last night. He climbed down into the broken little boat tied to the short sandalwood tree on the riverbank, placed the oar, tucked the tobacco basket under the bow, and then used a sorghum broom without a handle to wipe away the frost from the boat's beam.

"I wonder which little devil cut the boat rope!" When he went to untie the rope, he discovered that half of the thick hemp rope had been cut with two knife marks.

The small boat drifted towards the Sandbar at Temple Mountain, gradually drifting into West Tai Lake. The wind whipped up white waves, crashing head-on into the boat, causing the hull to struggle and race like a runaway horse in the boundless, treacherous waves. Ye Ya San gripped the oar, gritted his teeth, and trembled at the stern. The waves crashed against the boat, splashing him with water, soaking his tattered cotton-padded coat.

The sun followed the small boat, climbing out of the depression and slowly rising into the sky. But as soon as it emerged from the mountain hollow, the sunlight was diluted by the wind, pale like the face of a lung patient, so dejected and defeated, as if deliberately mocking Ye Ya San, appearing and disappearing in the clouds.

He rowed the boat past Three Mountains Dam and saw a patch of withered grey reeds in the distance. He quickly rowed a few more strokes, and the boat reached the edge of the reeds. He warmed his hands, which were frozen as if his fingers had been amputated, and he felt a bit numb.

He steered the boat close to the reeds, remembered where he had set the "fairy trap" yesterday, and began to collect them, one, two, three...

"Eh! Why isn't a single one set off? Could it be that no one came even in such cold weather yesterday?" He thought to himself, feeling a little disappointed!

Last night, he had placed a total of twenty bamboo bows here, but eighteen were empty, capturing only two wild ducks, both male coots. He threw all the ropes and bamboo bows into the cabin, sighed, and sat on the boat's beam to smoke.

The reeds rustled in the wind, the sound so desolate and mournful that it sounded to his ears like countless people weeping for hunger and cold, and it seemed as if he could even hear the voices of his mother, wife, and children.

Dejectedly, he rowed the boat out of the reeds and headed towards Luanmen, but at this time the wind was even stronger than before, the sun had hidden itself, the sky was painted with a heavy leaden color, and the earth had turned grey and dark, as if about to collapse. At the same time, Ye Ya San's heart felt as heavy as if it had been filled with lead, and his mind was as dark as if it had been covered with grey paper—

The Oppressive City Sky 214

— Huang

Once you come to the city, even the gifts of nature that you enjoy in the countryside are stripped away. In a cramped attic room, you can't see a single ray of sunlight all day long. When you open the window and look out, you are met with three sides of sheer, grey walls, blocking your view. The small room is like being stuck in a deep well. Even when you look up at the sky, it's only a somber, narrow corner, completely losing its original lofty and bright appearance. At night, there is no moon, no stars, only boundless darkness.

In such circumstances, people feel suffocated and gloomy. If it's also drizzling outside, then such a mood is most unbearable.

For the past few days, the sky has been overcast, like a sheet of lead. Even at midday, the sky looks almost like dusk. The electric lights that are on all day long, with their dim, yellow light, only add to the depression in one's heart. Sitting isn't right, standing isn't right, so you can only watch the swirling rain threads by the window, but that still can't cover up the loneliness in your heart. At night, the dripping rain sounds even more desolate, and as the drops fall on the bed, you think about completely vague things, vague things that you don't even know why they float to the surface of your mind.

On the way home, I encountered rain again. Standing under the glass eaves of a store to take shelter, I quietly watched the crowds of people coming and going like dark clouds. Most of them were hunched over, walking at an angle, and the neon lights reflected on the puddles on the asphalt road like winding red snakes. The tram was like a giant beast crawling out of the water, and the streetlights were like giant eyes filled with tears, coldly hanging over the city streets in the rain. Although this was the first time I had encountered this scene, I extremely detested it, so decadent and embarrassing!

The genius French painter Van Gogh once said, "Thinking about the sun in the south in a rainy hometown makes one weary." I deeply experience the feelings of this wandering artist.

Originally, it should be the season for snowfall now, but it's still drizzling day after day, night after night, how annoying the weather is! I like the purity of snow, and even more, I like the sun. It warms me, inspires me, and gives me light, but the darkness covers it, throwing us into the abyss. When will we see the sun? At this moment, I couldn't help but pray like this.

Li Shude (940) 7:30 AM to 8:30 AM

Xu Mei Sent a Poem: After Reading, Left My Eyebrows Raised

A chance encounter in a spring boudoir, exceeding expectations. At first sight, I doubted it was a dream, and we sadly asked each other about our years. This feeling is almost like that again. At that time, official matters urged me on, and I regret not being able to chat freely. At the beginning of summer, I planned to accompany my host to visit my hometown, but you had already set sail for Lu River. Returning after the Dragon Boat Festival, I unfolded and read your letter. Your thoughts and feelings were earnest and sincere, recounting your current situation and recalling the past joys, which made me even more emotional. You have accumulated much learning and literature, and I have long planned to be among the literati in the capital. It is certainly better to be at the tail of an ox than at the head of a chicken. As for the current situation of private tutoring, it is generally the same. A blue carpet (job) can last a long time or not, only you can judge the times and handle it well. I have been travelling for many years. My aging mother leans on the door every day, longing for my return. But because I am empty-handed, I cannot return. The heroic spirit of the past has gradually faded away in the tedious and melancholy world. I send you these four recent poems, and you may be surprised by their decline.

Opening passage: "Dream of the Red Chamber: Qingwen is Expelled"

Charming and captivating Qingwen, diligently serving in the Yi Hong Courtyard. It is hateful, that Mother Wang Shanbao slanders her. Saying that, Qingwen is clever and delicate. She is, a cherry-mouthed girl with a sharp tongue, presumptuous and accustomed to bullying people. The Madam hears, and believes it to be true. Thinking of the past, she is filled with anger. She scolds, "That hussy is too flirtatious and light-boned. Could it be, that I saw her in the garden that day, with her snake waist, narrow shoulders, and sly, slippery eyes? Moreover, 'satisfied with warmth, one thinks of lust' is an old saying. It's hard to guarantee that Baoyu won't be seduced." Thinking of the future, she feels concerned. She immediately orders a maid to summon Qingwen. Qingwen is, suffering from an illness and feeling upset, lying weakly in bed alone with her quilt. Hearing the maid's summons, she trembles with fear. She has no choice but to throw off the covers, put on her clothes, and force herself to get up. The Madam sees, and her heart is filled with hatred. Seeing her, with her hairpin half-askew and her temples half-loose, she says, "What a 'sickly beauty of the West.' I see that you are frivolous and not a good person. I have heard all about your actions. I will report to the Grand Madam and expel you, you demon!" Pitiful Qingwen, although she has a hundred mouths, she cannot defend herself. Her heart is filled with resentment and tears stain her lapel. She is, intelligent and aware of the plot within. She realizes that someone is secretly plotting against her. She covers her face and cries as she goes to the garden. She staggers, her footsteps faltering. Thinking, in the past I was favored by Baoyu, but who knew, mending the coat was still in vain. Grieved all day, her illness worsens. Not a drop of rice can she swallow. With unkempt hair and a dirty face, she is emaciated. A fierce old woman drags her out the door. Slowly, her lingering illness draws her near the Yellow Springs.

Movie

Talking About the Scenes in "Triumphant Return" 220

"Triumphant Return" has a luxurious parade scene, with banners covering the sky and stretching for miles. Dragon formations, lion formations, bamboo bands, stilt walkers, all kinds of shapes and colors, creating an unprecedented lively scene.

"Triumphant Return" has a magnificent dam opening scene, with a grand setting, tense atmosphere, numerous actors, and tragic performance, comparable to "Long Live Freedom."

"Triumphant Return" has a scene of waterwheels lined up in a formation. Thirty to forty waterwheels are seen connected together, the sound of the leaves is like a bell, and the water splashes everywhere. The magnificence of the scene and the beauty of the picture have never been seen in Chinese and Western films.

"Triumphant Return" has a vast farmland scene, with thousands of farmers fighting each other for water, the scene is very tragic, and the atmosphere is extremely serious. It is a realistic painting of the countryside, a page of the peasant's bloody history.

"Triumphant Return" has a solemn and magnificent Dragon King Temple scene, where several scenes of conflict between new and old ideas, the struggle of old forces, the tension of the situation, and the seriousness of the situation are fully demonstrated, revealing the darkness of rural society and the crisis lurking among young farmers that is about to erupt.

In short, every scene in "Triumphant Return" is magnificent, grand, tense, piercing, and beautiful.

Miscellaneous News About the Revival of "The Government Inspector" 223

"The Government Inspector" was previously performed at Jincheng, and many people regretted not being able to see it. It will be revived at the Central Grand Theatre, with ticket prices reduced to three, five, and eight 角. The dates are the 22nd, 23rd, and 24th of this month. This is also good news for theater fans.

It is rumored that the script of "The Government Inspector" has been revised for the revival. However, according to reporters, this is not true. However, the positions of the supporting actors have been completely rearranged, the long stage has been removed, and more gimmicks have been added to wash away the dull atmosphere.

Director of the Postal Bureau Gu Menghu went to Beijing on official business. It is said that he has sent a telegram to invite him. If he cannot spare time from his official duties, he will appoint Shan Xuliang to act on his behalf.

The rehearsal time for this revival is the 19th, 20th, and 21st. To save time, it has been decided to change the previous method of rehearsing by act to rehearsing by scene to achieve twice the result with half the effort.

Yin Xiucen, Jin Shan, Li Dizhi, and Zhu Mingxian have been busy filming in various places recently, but they are still very enthusiastic about the performance of "The Government Inspector". They have been urging the rehearsal by telephone every day.

Local gentlemen Pi Buqing and Liu Mang are busy with important matters and cannot participate in the revival. They have specially hired Mr. Xu Tao, an old stage actor who has directed many plays, to play this role. Xu is as thin as a skeleton and is short, making him a suitable and enjoyable candidate.

Wang Ying recently bought a Japanese heating stove. She sits on the floor every day, carefully studying the script by the stove. She once said to people that this kind of life is an ideal life.

In winter, some are lucky and some are not. County Governor Gu Eryi almost died of gas poisoning at home the other day. After waking up, he boasted to people that because "The Government Inspector" had not yet been revived, he did not die resolutely.

Lan Ping recently suffered from a cold. Because the revival is imminent, others are quite anxious. Lan always gets sick before each performance, but as soon as the performance officially starts, she always recovers quickly. Therefore, she herself is quite relieved, and often says it's okay, it's okay.
